# Content Selection - Crawl4AI Documentation

Content Selection
=================

Crawl4AI provides multiple ways to select and filter specific content from webpages. Learn how to precisely target the content you need.

CSS Selectors
-------------

The simplest way to extract specific content:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) # Extract specific content using CSS selector [](#__codelineno-0-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-3)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-4)     css_selector=".main-article"  # Target main article content [](#__codelineno-0-5) ) [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Multiple selectors [](#__codelineno-0-8) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-9)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-10)     css_selector="article h1, article .content"  # Target heading and content [](#__codelineno-0-11) )`

Content Filtering
-----------------

Control what content is included or excluded:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     # Content thresholds [](#__codelineno-1-4)     word_count_threshold=10,        # Minimum words per block [](#__codelineno-1-5) [](#__codelineno-1-6)     # Tag exclusions [](#__codelineno-1-7)     excluded_tags=['form', 'header', 'footer', 'nav'], [](#__codelineno-1-8) [](#__codelineno-1-9)     # Link filtering [](#__codelineno-1-10)     exclude_external_links=True,    # Remove external links [](#__codelineno-1-11)     exclude_social_media_links=True,  # Remove social media links [](#__codelineno-1-12) [](#__codelineno-1-13)     # Media filtering [](#__codelineno-1-14)     exclude_external_images=True   # Remove external images [](#__codelineno-1-15) )`

Iframe Content
--------------

Process content inside iframes:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     process_iframes=True,  # Extract iframe content [](#__codelineno-2-4)     remove_overlay_elements=True  # Remove popups/modals that might block iframes [](#__codelineno-2-5) )`

Structured Content Selection
----------------------------

### Using LLMs for Smart Selection

Use LLMs to intelligently extract specific types of content:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) from pydantic import BaseModel [](#__codelineno-3-2) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-3-3) [](#__codelineno-3-4) class ArticleContent(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-3-5)     title: str [](#__codelineno-3-6)     main_points: List[str] [](#__codelineno-3-7)     conclusion: str [](#__codelineno-3-8) [](#__codelineno-3-9) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-3-10)     provider="ollama/nemotron",  # Works with any supported LLM [](#__codelineno-3-11)     schema=ArticleContent.schema(), [](#__codelineno-3-12)     instruction="Extract the main article title, key points, and conclusion" [](#__codelineno-3-13) ) [](#__codelineno-3-14) [](#__codelineno-3-15) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-16)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-3-17)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-3-18) ) [](#__codelineno-3-19) article = json.loads(result.extracted_content)`

### Pattern-Based Selection

For repeated content patterns (like product listings, news feeds):

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-4-2) [](#__codelineno-4-3) schema = { [](#__codelineno-4-4)     "name": "News Articles", [](#__codelineno-4-5)     "baseSelector": "article.news-item",  # Repeated element [](#__codelineno-4-6)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-4-7)         {"name": "headline", "selector": "h2", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-4-8)         {"name": "summary", "selector": ".summary", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-4-9)         {"name": "category", "selector": ".category", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-4-10)         { [](#__codelineno-4-11)             "name": "metadata", [](#__codelineno-4-12)             "type": "nested", [](#__codelineno-4-13)             "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-4-14)                 {"name": "author", "selector": ".author", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-4-15)                 {"name": "date", "selector": ".date", "type": "text"} [](#__codelineno-4-16)             ] [](#__codelineno-4-17)         } [](#__codelineno-4-18)     ] [](#__codelineno-4-19) } [](#__codelineno-4-20) [](#__codelineno-4-21) strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema) [](#__codelineno-4-22) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-23)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-24)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-4-25) ) [](#__codelineno-4-26) articles = json.loads(result.extracted_content)`

Domain-Based Filtering
----------------------

Control content based on domains:

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-5-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-5-3)     exclude_domains=["ads.com", "tracker.com"], [](#__codelineno-5-4)     exclude_social_media_domains=["facebook.com", "twitter.com"],  # Custom social media domains to exclude [](#__codelineno-5-5)     exclude_social_media_links=True [](#__codelineno-5-6) )`

Media Selection
---------------

Select specific types of media:

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-6-2) [](#__codelineno-6-3) # Access different media types [](#__codelineno-6-4) images = result.media["images"]  # List of image details [](#__codelineno-6-5) videos = result.media["videos"]  # List of video details [](#__codelineno-6-6) audios = result.media["audios"]  # List of audio details [](#__codelineno-6-7) [](#__codelineno-6-8) # Image with metadata [](#__codelineno-6-9) for image in images: [](#__codelineno-6-10)     print(f"URL: {image['src']}") [](#__codelineno-6-11)     print(f"Alt text: {image['alt']}") [](#__codelineno-6-12)     print(f"Description: {image['desc']}") [](#__codelineno-6-13)     print(f"Relevance score: {image['score']}")`

Comprehensive Example
---------------------

Here's how to combine different selection methods:

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) async def extract_article_content(url: str): [](#__codelineno-7-2)     # Define structured extraction [](#__codelineno-7-3)     article_schema = { [](#__codelineno-7-4)         "name": "Article", [](#__codelineno-7-5)         "baseSelector": "article.main", [](#__codelineno-7-6)         "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-7-7)             {"name": "title", "selector": "h1", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-7-8)             {"name": "content", "selector": ".content", "type": "text"} [](#__codelineno-7-9)         ] [](#__codelineno-7-10)     } [](#__codelineno-7-11) [](#__codelineno-7-12)     # Define LLM extraction [](#__codelineno-7-13)     class ArticleAnalysis(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-7-14)         key_points: List[str] [](#__codelineno-7-15)         sentiment: str [](#__codelineno-7-16)         category: str [](#__codelineno-7-17) [](#__codelineno-7-18)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-7-19)         # Get structured content [](#__codelineno-7-20)         pattern_result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-21)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-7-22)             extraction_strategy=JsonCssExtractionStrategy(article_schema), [](#__codelineno-7-23)             word_count_threshold=10, [](#__codelineno-7-24)             excluded_tags=['nav', 'footer'], [](#__codelineno-7-25)             exclude_external_links=True [](#__codelineno-7-26)         ) [](#__codelineno-7-27) [](#__codelineno-7-28)         # Get semantic analysis [](#__codelineno-7-29)         analysis_result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-30)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-7-31)             extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-7-32)                 provider="ollama/nemotron", [](#__codelineno-7-33)                 schema=ArticleAnalysis.schema(), [](#__codelineno-7-34)                 instruction="Analyze the article content" [](#__codelineno-7-35)             ) [](#__codelineno-7-36)         ) [](#__codelineno-7-37) [](#__codelineno-7-38)         # Combine results [](#__codelineno-7-39)         return { [](#__codelineno-7-40)             "article": json.loads(pattern_result.extracted_content), [](#__codelineno-7-41)             "analysis": json.loads(analysis_result.extracted_content), [](#__codelineno-7-42)             "media": pattern_result.media [](#__codelineno-7-43)         }`

# Cache Modes - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI Cache System and Migration Guide
=========================================

Overview
--------

Starting from version 0.5.0, Crawl4AI introduces a new caching system that replaces the old boolean flags with a more intuitive `CacheMode` enum. This change simplifies cache control and makes the behavior more predictable.

Old vs New Approach
-------------------

### Old Way (Deprecated)

The old system used multiple boolean flags: - `bypass_cache`: Skip cache entirely - `disable_cache`: Disable all caching - `no_cache_read`: Don't read from cache - `no_cache_write`: Don't write to cache

### New Way (Recommended)

The new system uses a single `CacheMode` enum: - `CacheMode.ENABLED`: Normal caching (read/write) - `CacheMode.DISABLED`: No caching at all - `CacheMode.READ_ONLY`: Only read from cache - `CacheMode.WRITE_ONLY`: Only write to cache - `CacheMode.BYPASS`: Skip cache for this operation

Migration Example
-----------------

### Old Code (Deprecated)

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) async def use_proxy(): [](#__codelineno-0-5)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-6)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-7)             url="https://www.nbcnews.com/business", [](#__codelineno-0-8)             bypass_cache=True  # Old way [](#__codelineno-0-9)         ) [](#__codelineno-0-10)         print(len(result.markdown)) [](#__codelineno-0-11) [](#__codelineno-0-12) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-0-13)     await use_proxy() [](#__codelineno-0-14) [](#__codelineno-0-15) if __name__ == "__main__": [](#__codelineno-0-16)     asyncio.run(main())`

### New Code (Recommended)

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-1-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler, CacheMode  # Import CacheMode [](#__codelineno-1-3) [](#__codelineno-1-4) async def use_proxy(): [](#__codelineno-1-5)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-6)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-7)             url="https://www.nbcnews.com/business", [](#__codelineno-1-8)             cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS  # New way [](#__codelineno-1-9)         ) [](#__codelineno-1-10)         print(len(result.markdown)) [](#__codelineno-1-11) [](#__codelineno-1-12) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-1-13)     await use_proxy() [](#__codelineno-1-14) [](#__codelineno-1-15) if __name__ == "__main__": [](#__codelineno-1-16)     asyncio.run(main())`

Common Migration Patterns
-------------------------

| Old Flag | New Mode |
| --- | --- |
| `bypass_cache=True` | `cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS` |
| `disable_cache=True` | `cache_mode=CacheMode.DISABLED` |
| `no_cache_read=True` | `cache_mode=CacheMode.WRITE_ONLY` |
| `no_cache_write=True` | `cache_mode=CacheMode.READ_ONLY` |

Suppressing Deprecation Warnings
--------------------------------

If you need time to migrate, you can temporarily suppress deprecation warnings:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) # In your config.py [](#__codelineno-2-2) SHOW_DEPRECATION_WARNINGS = False`

# Content Processing - Crawl4AI Documentation

Content Processing
==================

Crawl4AI provides powerful content processing capabilities that help you extract clean, relevant content from web pages. This guide covers content cleaning, media handling, link analysis, and metadata extraction.

Content Cleaning
----------------

### Understanding Clean Content

When crawling web pages, you often encounter a lot of noise - advertisements, navigation menus, footers, popups, and other irrelevant content. Crawl4AI automatically cleans this noise using several approaches:

1.  **Basic Cleaning**: Removes unwanted HTML elements and attributes
2.  **Content Relevance**: Identifies and preserves meaningful content blocks
3.  **Layout Analysis**: Understands page structure to identify main content areas

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-3)     word_count_threshold=10,        # Remove blocks with fewer words [](#__codelineno-0-4)     excluded_tags=['form', 'nav'],  # Remove specific HTML tags [](#__codelineno-0-5)     remove_overlay_elements=True    # Remove popups/modals [](#__codelineno-0-6) ) [](#__codelineno-0-7) [](#__codelineno-0-8) # Get clean content [](#__codelineno-0-9) print(result.cleaned_html)  # Cleaned HTML [](#__codelineno-0-10) print(result.markdown)      # Clean markdown version`

### Fit Markdown: Smart Content Extraction

One of Crawl4AI's most powerful features is `fit_markdown`. This feature uses advanced heuristics to identify and extract the main content from a webpage while excluding irrelevant elements.

#### How Fit Markdown Works

*   Analyzes content density and distribution
*   Identifies content patterns and structures
*   Removes boilerplate content (headers, footers, sidebars)
*   Preserves the most relevant content blocks
*   Maintains content hierarchy and formatting

#### Perfect For:

*   Blog posts and articles
*   News content
*   Documentation pages
*   Any page with a clear main content area

#### Not Recommended For:

*   E-commerce product listings
*   Search results pages
*   Social media feeds
*   Pages with multiple equal-weight content sections

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-1-2) [](#__codelineno-1-3) # Get the most relevant content [](#__codelineno-1-4) main_content = result.fit_markdown [](#__codelineno-1-5) [](#__codelineno-1-6) # Compare with regular markdown [](#__codelineno-1-7) all_content = result.markdown [](#__codelineno-1-8) [](#__codelineno-1-9) print(f"Fit Markdown Length: {len(main_content)}") [](#__codelineno-1-10) print(f"Regular Markdown Length: {len(all_content)}")`

#### Example Use Case

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def extract_article_content(url: str) -> str: [](#__codelineno-2-2)     """Extract main article content from a blog or news site.""" [](#__codelineno-2-3)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-4)         result = await crawler.arun(url=url) [](#__codelineno-2-5) [](#__codelineno-2-6)         # fit_markdown will focus on the article content, [](#__codelineno-2-7)         # excluding navigation, ads, and other distractions [](#__codelineno-2-8)         return result.fit_markdown`

Media Processing
----------------

Crawl4AI provides comprehensive media extraction and analysis capabilities. It automatically detects and processes various types of media elements while maintaining their context and relevance.

### Image Processing

The library handles various image scenarios, including: - Regular images - Lazy-loaded images - Background images - Responsive images - Image metadata and context

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-3-2) [](#__codelineno-3-3) for image in result.media["images"]: [](#__codelineno-3-4)     # Each image includes rich metadata [](#__codelineno-3-5)     print(f"Source: {image['src']}") [](#__codelineno-3-6)     print(f"Alt text: {image['alt']}") [](#__codelineno-3-7)     print(f"Description: {image['desc']}") [](#__codelineno-3-8)     print(f"Context: {image['context']}")  # Surrounding text [](#__codelineno-3-9)     print(f"Relevance score: {image['score']}")  # 0-10 score`

### Handling Lazy-Loaded Content

Crawl4aai already handles lazy loading for media elements. You can also customize the wait time for lazy-loaded content:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-3)     wait_for="css:img[data-src]",  # Wait for lazy images [](#__codelineno-4-4)     delay_before_return_html=2.0   # Additional wait time [](#__codelineno-4-5) )`

### Video and Audio Content

The library extracts video and audio elements with their metadata:

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) # Process videos [](#__codelineno-5-2) for video in result.media["videos"]: [](#__codelineno-5-3)     print(f"Video source: {video['src']}") [](#__codelineno-5-4)     print(f"Type: {video['type']}") [](#__codelineno-5-5)     print(f"Duration: {video.get('duration')}") [](#__codelineno-5-6)     print(f"Thumbnail: {video.get('poster')}") [](#__codelineno-5-7) [](#__codelineno-5-8) # Process audio [](#__codelineno-5-9) for audio in result.media["audios"]: [](#__codelineno-5-10)     print(f"Audio source: {audio['src']}") [](#__codelineno-5-11)     print(f"Type: {audio['type']}") [](#__codelineno-5-12)     print(f"Duration: {audio.get('duration')}")`

Link Analysis
-------------

Crawl4AI provides sophisticated link analysis capabilities, helping you understand the relationship between pages and identify important navigation patterns.

### Link Classification

The library automatically categorizes links into: - Internal links (same domain) - External links (different domains) - Social media links - Navigation links - Content links

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-6-2) [](#__codelineno-6-3) # Analyze internal links [](#__codelineno-6-4) for link in result.links["internal"]: [](#__codelineno-6-5)     print(f"Internal: {link['href']}") [](#__codelineno-6-6)     print(f"Link text: {link['text']}") [](#__codelineno-6-7)     print(f"Context: {link['context']}")  # Surrounding text [](#__codelineno-6-8)     print(f"Type: {link['type']}")  # nav, content, etc. [](#__codelineno-6-9) [](#__codelineno-6-10) # Analyze external links [](#__codelineno-6-11) for link in result.links["external"]: [](#__codelineno-6-12)     print(f"External: {link['href']}") [](#__codelineno-6-13)     print(f"Domain: {link['domain']}") [](#__codelineno-6-14)     print(f"Type: {link['type']}")`

### Smart Link Filtering

Control which links are included in the results:

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-7-3)     exclude_external_links=True,          # Remove external links [](#__codelineno-7-4)     exclude_social_media_links=True,      # Remove social media links [](#__codelineno-7-5)     exclude_social_media_domains=[                # Custom social media domains [](#__codelineno-7-6)         "facebook.com", "twitter.com", "instagram.com" [](#__codelineno-7-7)     ], [](#__codelineno-7-8)     exclude_domains=["ads.example.com"]   # Exclude specific domains [](#__codelineno-7-9) )`

Metadata Extraction
-------------------

Crawl4AI automatically extracts and processes page metadata, providing valuable information about the content:

`[](#__codelineno-8-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-8-2) [](#__codelineno-8-3) metadata = result.metadata [](#__codelineno-8-4) print(f"Title: {metadata['title']}") [](#__codelineno-8-5) print(f"Description: {metadata['description']}") [](#__codelineno-8-6) print(f"Keywords: {metadata['keywords']}") [](#__codelineno-8-7) print(f"Author: {metadata['author']}") [](#__codelineno-8-8) print(f"Published Date: {metadata['published_date']}") [](#__codelineno-8-9) print(f"Modified Date: {metadata['modified_date']}") [](#__codelineno-8-10) print(f"Language: {metadata['language']}")`

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Use Fit Markdown for Articles**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-9-1) # Perfect for blog posts, news articles, documentation [](#__codelineno-9-2) content = result.fit_markdown`
    
2.  **Handle Media Appropriately**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-10-1) # Filter by relevance score [](#__codelineno-10-2) relevant_images = [ [](#__codelineno-10-3)     img for img in result.media["images"] [](#__codelineno-10-4)     if img['score'] > 5 [](#__codelineno-10-5) ]`
    
3.  **Combine Link Analysis with Content**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-11-1) # Get content links with context [](#__codelineno-11-2) content_links = [ [](#__codelineno-11-3)     link for link in result.links["internal"] [](#__codelineno-11-4)     if link['type'] == 'content' [](#__codelineno-11-5) ]`
    
4.  **Clean Content with Purpose**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-12-1) # Customize cleaning based on your needs [](#__codelineno-12-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-12-3)     url=url, [](#__codelineno-12-4)     word_count_threshold=20,      # Adjust based on content type [](#__codelineno-12-5)     keep_data_attributes=False,   # Remove data attributes [](#__codelineno-12-6)     process_iframes=True         # Include iframe content [](#__codelineno-12-7) )`

# Session Management - Crawl4AI Documentation

Session Management
==================

Session management in Crawl4AI allows you to maintain state across multiple requests and handle complex multi-page crawling tasks, particularly useful for dynamic websites.

Basic Session Usage
-------------------

Use `session_id` to maintain state between requests:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-2)     session_id = "my_session" [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4)     # First request [](#__codelineno-0-5)     result1 = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-6)         url="https://example.com/page1", [](#__codelineno-0-7)         session_id=session_id [](#__codelineno-0-8)     ) [](#__codelineno-0-9) [](#__codelineno-0-10)     # Subsequent request using same session [](#__codelineno-0-11)     result2 = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-12)         url="https://example.com/page2", [](#__codelineno-0-13)         session_id=session_id [](#__codelineno-0-14)     ) [](#__codelineno-0-15) [](#__codelineno-0-16)     # Clean up when done [](#__codelineno-0-17)     await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id)`

Dynamic Content with Sessions
-----------------------------

Here's a real-world example of crawling GitHub commits across multiple pages:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) async def crawl_dynamic_content(): [](#__codelineno-1-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-3)         url = "https://github.com/microsoft/TypeScript/commits/main" [](#__codelineno-1-4)         session_id = "typescript_commits_session" [](#__codelineno-1-5)         all_commits = [] [](#__codelineno-1-6) [](#__codelineno-1-7)         # Define navigation JavaScript [](#__codelineno-1-8)         js_next_page = """ [](#__codelineno-1-9)         const button = document.querySelector('a[data-testid="pagination-next-button"]'); [](#__codelineno-1-10)         if (button) button.click(); [](#__codelineno-1-11)         """ [](#__codelineno-1-12) [](#__codelineno-1-13)         # Define wait condition [](#__codelineno-1-14)         wait_for = """() => { [](#__codelineno-1-15)             const commits = document.querySelectorAll('li.Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 h4'); [](#__codelineno-1-16)             if (commits.length === 0) return false; [](#__codelineno-1-17)             const firstCommit = commits[0].textContent.trim(); [](#__codelineno-1-18)             return firstCommit !== window.firstCommit; [](#__codelineno-1-19)         }""" [](#__codelineno-1-20) [](#__codelineno-1-21)         # Define extraction schema [](#__codelineno-1-22)         schema = { [](#__codelineno-1-23)             "name": "Commit Extractor", [](#__codelineno-1-24)             "baseSelector": "li.Box-sc-g0xbh4-0", [](#__codelineno-1-25)             "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-26)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-27)                     "name": "title", [](#__codelineno-1-28)                     "selector": "h4.markdown-title", [](#__codelineno-1-29)                     "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-1-30)                     "transform": "strip", [](#__codelineno-1-31)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-32)             ], [](#__codelineno-1-33)         } [](#__codelineno-1-34)         extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema) [](#__codelineno-1-35) [](#__codelineno-1-36)         # Crawl multiple pages [](#__codelineno-1-37)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-1-38)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-39)                 url=url, [](#__codelineno-1-40)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-1-41)                 extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-1-42)                 js_code=js_next_page if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-1-43)                 wait_for=wait_for if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-1-44)                 js_only=page > 0, [](#__codelineno-1-45)                 cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-1-46)             ) [](#__codelineno-1-47) [](#__codelineno-1-48)             if result.success: [](#__codelineno-1-49)                 commits = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-1-50)                 all_commits.extend(commits) [](#__codelineno-1-51)                 print(f"Page {page + 1}: Found {len(commits)} commits") [](#__codelineno-1-52) [](#__codelineno-1-53)         # Clean up session [](#__codelineno-1-54)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id) [](#__codelineno-1-55)         return all_commits`

Session Best Practices
----------------------

1.  **Session Naming**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) # Use descriptive session IDs [](#__codelineno-2-2) session_id = "login_flow_session" [](#__codelineno-2-3) session_id = "product_catalog_session"`
    
2.  **Resource Management**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) try: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     # Your crawling code [](#__codelineno-3-3)     pass [](#__codelineno-3-4) finally: [](#__codelineno-3-5)     # Always clean up sessions [](#__codelineno-3-6)     await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id)`
    
3.  **State Management**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) # First page: login [](#__codelineno-4-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-3)     url="https://example.com/login", [](#__codelineno-4-4)     session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-4-5)     js_code="document.querySelector('form').submit();" [](#__codelineno-4-6) ) [](#__codelineno-4-7) [](#__codelineno-4-8) # Second page: verify login success [](#__codelineno-4-9) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-10)     url="https://example.com/dashboard", [](#__codelineno-4-11)     session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-4-12)     wait_for="css:.user-profile"  # Wait for authenticated content [](#__codelineno-4-13) )`
    

Common Use Cases
----------------

1.  **Authentication Flows**
2.  **Pagination Handling**
3.  **Form Submissions**
4.  **Multi-step Processes**
5.  **Dynamic Content Navigation**

# Hooks & Auth - Crawl4AI Documentation

Hooks & Auth for AsyncWebCrawler
================================

Crawl4AI's AsyncWebCrawler allows you to customize the behavior of the web crawler using hooks. Hooks are asynchronous functions that are called at specific points in the crawling process, allowing you to modify the crawler's behavior or perform additional actions. This example demonstrates how to use various hooks to customize the asynchronous crawling process.

Example: Using Crawler Hooks with AsyncWebCrawler
-------------------------------------------------

Let's see how we can customize the AsyncWebCrawler using hooks! In this example, we'll:

1.  Configure the browser when it's created.
2.  Add custom headers before navigating to the URL.
3.  Log the current URL after navigation.
4.  Perform actions after JavaScript execution.
5.  Log the length of the HTML before returning it.

### Hook Definitions

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-0-3) from crawl4ai.async_crawler_strategy import AsyncPlaywrightCrawlerStrategy [](#__codelineno-0-4) from playwright.async_api import Page, Browser, BrowserContext [](#__codelineno-0-5) [](#__codelineno-0-6) async def on_browser_created(browser: Browser): [](#__codelineno-0-7)     print("[HOOK] on_browser_created") [](#__codelineno-0-8)     # Example customization: set browser viewport size [](#__codelineno-0-9)     context = await browser.new_context(viewport={'width': 1920, 'height': 1080}) [](#__codelineno-0-10)     page = await context.new_page() [](#__codelineno-0-11) [](#__codelineno-0-12)     # Example customization: logging in to a hypothetical website [](#__codelineno-0-13)     await page.goto('https://example.com/login') [](#__codelineno-0-14)     await page.fill('input[name="username"]', 'testuser') [](#__codelineno-0-15)     await page.fill('input[name="password"]', 'password123') [](#__codelineno-0-16)     await page.click('button[type="submit"]') [](#__codelineno-0-17)     await page.wait_for_selector('#welcome') [](#__codelineno-0-18) [](#__codelineno-0-19)     # Add a custom cookie [](#__codelineno-0-20)     await context.add_cookies([{'name': 'test_cookie', 'value': 'cookie_value', 'url': 'https://example.com'}]) [](#__codelineno-0-21) [](#__codelineno-0-22)     await page.close() [](#__codelineno-0-23)     await context.close() [](#__codelineno-0-24) [](#__codelineno-0-25) async def before_goto(page: Page): [](#__codelineno-0-26)     print("[HOOK] before_goto") [](#__codelineno-0-27)     # Example customization: add custom headers [](#__codelineno-0-28)     await page.set_extra_http_headers({'X-Test-Header': 'test'}) [](#__codelineno-0-29) [](#__codelineno-0-30) async def after_goto(page: Page): [](#__codelineno-0-31)     print("[HOOK] after_goto") [](#__codelineno-0-32)     # Example customization: log the URL [](#__codelineno-0-33)     print(f"Current URL: {page.url}") [](#__codelineno-0-34) [](#__codelineno-0-35) async def on_execution_started(page: Page): [](#__codelineno-0-36)     print("[HOOK] on_execution_started") [](#__codelineno-0-37)     # Example customization: perform actions after JS execution [](#__codelineno-0-38)     await page.evaluate("console.log('Custom JS executed')") [](#__codelineno-0-39) [](#__codelineno-0-40) async def before_return_html(page: Page, html: str): [](#__codelineno-0-41)     print("[HOOK] before_return_html") [](#__codelineno-0-42)     # Example customization: log the HTML length [](#__codelineno-0-43)     print(f"HTML length: {len(html)}") [](#__codelineno-0-44)     return page`

### Using the Hooks with the AsyncWebCrawler

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-1-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-1-3) from crawl4ai.async_crawler_strategy import AsyncPlaywrightCrawlerStrategy [](#__codelineno-1-4) [](#__codelineno-1-5) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-1-6)     print("\n🔗 Using Crawler Hooks: Let's see how we can customize the AsyncWebCrawler using hooks!") [](#__codelineno-1-7) [](#__codelineno-1-8)     initial_cookies = [ [](#__codelineno-1-9)         {"name": "sessionId", "value": "abc123", "domain": ".example.com"}, [](#__codelineno-1-10)         {"name": "userId", "value": "12345", "domain": ".example.com"} [](#__codelineno-1-11)     ] [](#__codelineno-1-12)     crawler_strategy = AsyncPlaywrightCrawlerStrategy(verbose=True, cookies=initial_cookies) [](#__codelineno-1-13)     crawler_strategy.set_hook('on_browser_created', on_browser_created) [](#__codelineno-1-14)     crawler_strategy.set_hook('before_goto', before_goto) [](#__codelineno-1-15)     crawler_strategy.set_hook('after_goto', after_goto) [](#__codelineno-1-16)     crawler_strategy.set_hook('on_execution_started', on_execution_started) [](#__codelineno-1-17)     crawler_strategy.set_hook('before_return_html', before_return_html) [](#__codelineno-1-18) [](#__codelineno-1-19)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True, crawler_strategy=crawler_strategy) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-20)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-21)             url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-22)             js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-1-23)             wait_for="footer" [](#__codelineno-1-24)         ) [](#__codelineno-1-25) [](#__codelineno-1-26)     print("📦 Crawler Hooks result:") [](#__codelineno-1-27)     print(result) [](#__codelineno-1-28) [](#__codelineno-1-29) asyncio.run(main())`

### Explanation

*   `on_browser_created`: This hook is called when the Playwright browser is created. It sets up the browser context, logs in to a website, and adds a custom cookie.
*   `before_goto`: This hook is called right before Playwright navigates to the URL. It adds custom HTTP headers.
*   `after_goto`: This hook is called after Playwright navigates to the URL. It logs the current URL.
*   `on_execution_started`: This hook is called after any custom JavaScript is executed. It performs additional JavaScript actions.
*   `before_return_html`: This hook is called before returning the HTML content. It logs the length of the HTML content.

### Additional Ideas

*   **Handling authentication**: Use the `on_browser_created` hook to handle login processes or set authentication tokens.
*   **Dynamic header modification**: Modify headers based on the target URL or other conditions in the `before_goto` hook.
*   **Content verification**: Use the `after_goto` hook to verify that the expected content is present on the page.
*   **Custom JavaScript injection**: Inject and execute custom JavaScript using the `on_execution_started` hook.
*   **Content preprocessing**: Modify or analyze the HTML content in the `before_return_html` hook before it's returned.

By using these hooks, you can customize the behavior of the AsyncWebCrawler to suit your specific needs, including handling authentication, modifying requests, and preprocessing content.

* * *

---

# Proxy & Security - Crawl4AI Documentation

Proxy & Security
================

Configure proxy settings and enhance security features in Crawl4AI for reliable data extraction.

Basic Proxy Setup
-----------------

Simple proxy configuration:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) # Using proxy URL [](#__codelineno-0-2) async with AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-0-3)     proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080" [](#__codelineno-0-4) ) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-5)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Using SOCKS proxy [](#__codelineno-0-8) async with AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-0-9)     proxy="socks5://proxy.example.com:1080" [](#__codelineno-0-10) ) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-11)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com")`

Authenticated Proxy
-------------------

Use proxy with authentication:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) proxy_config = { [](#__codelineno-1-2)     "server": "http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     "username": "user", [](#__codelineno-1-4)     "password": "pass" [](#__codelineno-1-5) } [](#__codelineno-1-6) [](#__codelineno-1-7) async with AsyncWebCrawler(proxy_config=proxy_config) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-8)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com")`

Rotating Proxies
----------------

Example using a proxy rotation service:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def get_next_proxy(): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     # Your proxy rotation logic here [](#__codelineno-2-3)     return {"server": "http://next.proxy.com:8080"} [](#__codelineno-2-4) [](#__codelineno-2-5) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-6)     # Update proxy for each request [](#__codelineno-2-7)     for url in urls: [](#__codelineno-2-8)         proxy = await get_next_proxy() [](#__codelineno-2-9)         crawler.update_proxy(proxy) [](#__codelineno-2-10)         result = await crawler.arun(url=url)`

Custom Headers
--------------

Add security-related headers:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) headers = { [](#__codelineno-3-2)     "X-Forwarded-For": "203.0.113.195", [](#__codelineno-3-3)     "Accept-Language": "en-US,en;q=0.9", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     "Cache-Control": "no-cache", [](#__codelineno-3-5)     "Pragma": "no-cache" [](#__codelineno-3-6) } [](#__codelineno-3-7) [](#__codelineno-3-8) async with AsyncWebCrawler(headers=headers) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-3-9)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com")`

Combining with Magic Mode
-------------------------

For maximum protection, combine proxy with Magic Mode:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-4-2)     proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-4-3)     headers={"Accept-Language": "en-US"} [](#__codelineno-4-4) ) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-5)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-6)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-7)         magic=True  # Enable all anti-detection features [](#__codelineno-4-8)     )`

# Magic Mode - Crawl4AI Documentation

Magic Mode & Anti-Bot Protection
================================

Crawl4AI provides powerful anti-detection capabilities, with Magic Mode being the simplest and most comprehensive solution.

Magic Mode
----------

The easiest way to bypass anti-bot protections:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-4)         magic=True  # Enables all anti-detection features [](#__codelineno-0-5)     )`

Magic Mode automatically: - Masks browser automation signals - Simulates human-like behavior - Overrides navigator properties - Handles cookie consent popups - Manages browser fingerprinting - Randomizes timing patterns

Manual Anti-Bot Options
-----------------------

While Magic Mode is recommended, you can also configure individual anti-detection features:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     simulate_user=True,        # Simulate human behavior [](#__codelineno-1-4)     override_navigator=True    # Mask automation signals [](#__codelineno-1-5) )`

Note: When `magic=True` is used, you don't need to set these individual options.

Example: Handling Protected Sites
---------------------------------

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def crawl_protected_site(url: str): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(headless=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-3)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-4)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-2-5)             magic=True, [](#__codelineno-2-6)             remove_overlay_elements=True,  # Remove popups/modals [](#__codelineno-2-7)             page_timeout=60000            # Increased timeout for protection checks [](#__codelineno-2-8)         ) [](#__codelineno-2-9) [](#__codelineno-2-10)         return result.markdown if result.success else None`

* * *

# Session Management (Advanced) - Crawl4AI Documentation

Session-Based Crawling for Dynamic Content
==========================================

In modern web applications, content is often loaded dynamically without changing the URL. Examples include "Load More" buttons, infinite scrolling, or paginated content that updates via JavaScript. To effectively crawl such websites, Crawl4AI provides powerful session-based crawling capabilities.

This guide will explore advanced techniques for crawling dynamic content using Crawl4AI's session management features.

Understanding Session-Based Crawling
------------------------------------

Session-based crawling allows you to maintain a persistent browser session across multiple requests. This is crucial when:

1.  The content changes dynamically without URL changes
2.  You need to interact with the page (e.g., clicking buttons) between requests
3.  The site requires authentication or maintains state across pages

Crawl4AI's `AsyncWebCrawler` class supports session-based crawling through the `session_id` parameter and related methods.

Basic Concepts
--------------

Before diving into examples, let's review some key concepts:

*   **Session ID**: A unique identifier for a browsing session. Use the same `session_id` across multiple `arun` calls to maintain state.
*   **JavaScript Execution**: Use the `js_code` parameter to execute JavaScript on the page, such as clicking a "Load More" button.
*   **CSS Selectors**: Use these to target specific elements for extraction or interaction.
*   **Extraction Strategy**: Define how to extract structured data from the page.
*   **Wait Conditions**: Specify conditions to wait for before considering the page loaded.

Example 1: Basic Session-Based Crawling
---------------------------------------

Let's start with a basic example of session-based crawling:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler, CacheMode [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) async def basic_session_crawl(): [](#__codelineno-0-5)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-6)         session_id = "my_session" [](#__codelineno-0-7)         url = "https://example.com/dynamic-content" [](#__codelineno-0-8) [](#__codelineno-0-9)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-0-10)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-11)                 url=url, [](#__codelineno-0-12)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-0-13)                 js_code="document.querySelector('.load-more-button').click();" if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-0-14)                 css_selector=".content-item", [](#__codelineno-0-15)                 cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-0-16)             ) [](#__codelineno-0-17) [](#__codelineno-0-18)             print(f"Page {page + 1}: Found {result.extracted_content.count('.content-item')} items") [](#__codelineno-0-19) [](#__codelineno-0-20)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id) [](#__codelineno-0-21) [](#__codelineno-0-22) asyncio.run(basic_session_crawl())`

This example demonstrates: 1. Using a consistent `session_id` across multiple `arun` calls 2. Executing JavaScript to load more content after the first page 3. Using a CSS selector to extract specific content 4. Properly closing the session after crawling

Advanced Technique 1: Custom Execution Hooks
--------------------------------------------

Crawl4AI allows you to set custom hooks that execute at different stages of the crawling process. This is particularly useful for handling complex loading scenarios.

Here's an example that waits for new content to appear before proceeding:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) async def advanced_session_crawl_with_hooks(): [](#__codelineno-1-2)     first_commit = "" [](#__codelineno-1-3) [](#__codelineno-1-4)     async def on_execution_started(page): [](#__codelineno-1-5)         nonlocal first_commit [](#__codelineno-1-6)         try: [](#__codelineno-1-7)             while True: [](#__codelineno-1-8)                 await page.wait_for_selector("li.commit-item h4") [](#__codelineno-1-9)                 commit = await page.query_selector("li.commit-item h4") [](#__codelineno-1-10)                 commit = await commit.evaluate("(element) => element.textContent") [](#__codelineno-1-11)                 commit = commit.strip() [](#__codelineno-1-12)                 if commit and commit != first_commit: [](#__codelineno-1-13)                     first_commit = commit [](#__codelineno-1-14)                     break [](#__codelineno-1-15)                 await asyncio.sleep(0.5) [](#__codelineno-1-16)         except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-1-17)             print(f"Warning: New content didn't appear after JavaScript execution: {e}") [](#__codelineno-1-18) [](#__codelineno-1-19)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-20)         crawler.crawler_strategy.set_hook("on_execution_started", on_execution_started) [](#__codelineno-1-21) [](#__codelineno-1-22)         url = "https://github.com/example/repo/commits/main" [](#__codelineno-1-23)         session_id = "commit_session" [](#__codelineno-1-24)         all_commits = [] [](#__codelineno-1-25) [](#__codelineno-1-26)         js_next_page = """ [](#__codelineno-1-27)         const button = document.querySelector('a.pagination-next'); [](#__codelineno-1-28)         if (button) button.click(); [](#__codelineno-1-29)         """ [](#__codelineno-1-30) [](#__codelineno-1-31)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-1-32)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-33)                 url=url, [](#__codelineno-1-34)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-1-35)                 css_selector="li.commit-item", [](#__codelineno-1-36)                 js_code=js_next_page if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-1-37)                 cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS, [](#__codelineno-1-38)                 js_only=page > 0 [](#__codelineno-1-39)             ) [](#__codelineno-1-40) [](#__codelineno-1-41)             commits = result.extracted_content.select("li.commit-item") [](#__codelineno-1-42)             all_commits.extend(commits) [](#__codelineno-1-43)             print(f"Page {page + 1}: Found {len(commits)} commits") [](#__codelineno-1-44) [](#__codelineno-1-45)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id) [](#__codelineno-1-46)         print(f"Successfully crawled {len(all_commits)} commits across 3 pages") [](#__codelineno-1-47) [](#__codelineno-1-48) asyncio.run(advanced_session_crawl_with_hooks())`

This technique uses a custom `on_execution_started` hook to ensure new content has loaded before proceeding to the next step.

Advanced Technique 2: Integrated JavaScript Execution and Waiting
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Instead of using separate hooks, you can integrate the waiting logic directly into your JavaScript execution. This approach can be more concise and easier to manage for some scenarios.

Here's an example:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def integrated_js_and_wait_crawl(): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-3)         url = "https://github.com/example/repo/commits/main" [](#__codelineno-2-4)         session_id = "integrated_session" [](#__codelineno-2-5)         all_commits = [] [](#__codelineno-2-6) [](#__codelineno-2-7)         js_next_page_and_wait = """ [](#__codelineno-2-8)         (async () => { [](#__codelineno-2-9)             const getCurrentCommit = () => { [](#__codelineno-2-10)                 const commits = document.querySelectorAll('li.commit-item h4'); [](#__codelineno-2-11)                 return commits.length > 0 ? commits[0].textContent.trim() : null; [](#__codelineno-2-12)             }; [](#__codelineno-2-13) [](#__codelineno-2-14)             const initialCommit = getCurrentCommit(); [](#__codelineno-2-15)             const button = document.querySelector('a.pagination-next'); [](#__codelineno-2-16)             if (button) button.click(); [](#__codelineno-2-17) [](#__codelineno-2-18)             while (true) { [](#__codelineno-2-19)                 await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 100)); [](#__codelineno-2-20)                 const newCommit = getCurrentCommit(); [](#__codelineno-2-21)                 if (newCommit && newCommit !== initialCommit) { [](#__codelineno-2-22)                     break; [](#__codelineno-2-23)                 } [](#__codelineno-2-24)             } [](#__codelineno-2-25)         })(); [](#__codelineno-2-26)         """ [](#__codelineno-2-27) [](#__codelineno-2-28)         schema = { [](#__codelineno-2-29)             "name": "Commit Extractor", [](#__codelineno-2-30)             "baseSelector": "li.commit-item", [](#__codelineno-2-31)             "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-2-32)                 { [](#__codelineno-2-33)                     "name": "title", [](#__codelineno-2-34)                     "selector": "h4.commit-title", [](#__codelineno-2-35)                     "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-2-36)                     "transform": "strip", [](#__codelineno-2-37)                 }, [](#__codelineno-2-38)             ], [](#__codelineno-2-39)         } [](#__codelineno-2-40)         extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema, verbose=True) [](#__codelineno-2-41) [](#__codelineno-2-42)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-2-43)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-44)                 url=url, [](#__codelineno-2-45)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-2-46)                 css_selector="li.commit-item", [](#__codelineno-2-47)                 extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-2-48)                 js_code=js_next_page_and_wait if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-2-49)                 js_only=page > 0, [](#__codelineno-2-50)                 cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-2-51)             ) [](#__codelineno-2-52) [](#__codelineno-2-53)             commits = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-2-54)             all_commits.extend(commits) [](#__codelineno-2-55)             print(f"Page {page + 1}: Found {len(commits)} commits") [](#__codelineno-2-56) [](#__codelineno-2-57)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id) [](#__codelineno-2-58)         print(f"Successfully crawled {len(all_commits)} commits across 3 pages") [](#__codelineno-2-59) [](#__codelineno-2-60) asyncio.run(integrated_js_and_wait_crawl())`

This approach combines the JavaScript for clicking the "next" button and waiting for new content to load into a single script.

Advanced Technique 3: Using the `wait_for` Parameter
----------------------------------------------------

Crawl4AI provides a `wait_for` parameter that allows you to specify a condition to wait for before considering the page fully loaded. This can be particularly useful for dynamic content.

Here's an example:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) async def wait_for_parameter_crawl(): [](#__codelineno-3-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-3-3)         url = "https://github.com/example/repo/commits/main" [](#__codelineno-3-4)         session_id = "wait_for_session" [](#__codelineno-3-5)         all_commits = [] [](#__codelineno-3-6) [](#__codelineno-3-7)         js_next_page = """ [](#__codelineno-3-8)         const commits = document.querySelectorAll('li.commit-item h4'); [](#__codelineno-3-9)         if (commits.length > 0) { [](#__codelineno-3-10)             window.lastCommit = commits[0].textContent.trim(); [](#__codelineno-3-11)         } [](#__codelineno-3-12)         const button = document.querySelector('a.pagination-next'); [](#__codelineno-3-13)         if (button) button.click(); [](#__codelineno-3-14)         """ [](#__codelineno-3-15) [](#__codelineno-3-16)         wait_for = """() => { [](#__codelineno-3-17)             const commits = document.querySelectorAll('li.commit-item h4'); [](#__codelineno-3-18)             if (commits.length === 0) return false; [](#__codelineno-3-19)             const firstCommit = commits[0].textContent.trim(); [](#__codelineno-3-20)             return firstCommit !== window.lastCommit; [](#__codelineno-3-21)         }""" [](#__codelineno-3-22) [](#__codelineno-3-23)         schema = { [](#__codelineno-3-24)             "name": "Commit Extractor", [](#__codelineno-3-25)             "baseSelector": "li.commit-item", [](#__codelineno-3-26)             "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-3-27)                 { [](#__codelineno-3-28)                     "name": "title", [](#__codelineno-3-29)                     "selector": "h4.commit-title", [](#__codelineno-3-30)                     "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-3-31)                     "transform": "strip", [](#__codelineno-3-32)                 }, [](#__codelineno-3-33)             ], [](#__codelineno-3-34)         } [](#__codelineno-3-35)         extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema, verbose=True) [](#__codelineno-3-36) [](#__codelineno-3-37)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-3-38)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-39)                 url=url, [](#__codelineno-3-40)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-3-41)                 css_selector="li.commit-item", [](#__codelineno-3-42)                 extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-3-43)                 js_code=js_next_page if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-3-44)                 wait_for=wait_for if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-3-45)                 js_only=page > 0, [](#__codelineno-3-46)                 cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-3-47)             ) [](#__codelineno-3-48) [](#__codelineno-3-49)             commits = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-3-50)             all_commits.extend(commits) [](#__codelineno-3-51)             print(f"Page {page + 1}: Found {len(commits)} commits") [](#__codelineno-3-52) [](#__codelineno-3-53)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id) [](#__codelineno-3-54)         print(f"Successfully crawled {len(all_commits)} commits across 3 pages") [](#__codelineno-3-55) [](#__codelineno-3-56) asyncio.run(wait_for_parameter_crawl())`

This technique separates the JavaScript execution (clicking the "next" button) from the waiting condition, providing more flexibility and clarity in some scenarios.

Best Practices for Session-Based Crawling
-----------------------------------------

1.  **Use Unique Session IDs**: Ensure each crawling session has a unique `session_id` to prevent conflicts.
2.  **Close Sessions**: Always close sessions using `kill_session` when you're done to free up resources.
3.  **Handle Errors**: Implement proper error handling to deal with unexpected situations during crawling.
4.  **Respect Website Terms**: Ensure your crawling adheres to the website's terms of service and robots.txt file.
5.  **Implement Delays**: Add appropriate delays between requests to avoid overwhelming the target server.
6.  **Use Extraction Strategies**: Leverage `JsonCssExtractionStrategy` or other extraction strategies for structured data extraction.
7.  **Optimize JavaScript**: Keep your JavaScript execution concise and efficient to improve crawling speed.
8.  **Monitor Performance**: Keep an eye on memory usage and crawling speed, especially for long-running sessions.

Conclusion
----------

Session-based crawling with Crawl4AI provides powerful capabilities for handling dynamic content and complex web applications. By leveraging session management, JavaScript execution, and waiting strategies, you can effectively crawl and extract data from a wide range of modern websites.

Remember to use these techniques responsibly and in compliance with website policies and ethical web scraping practices.

For more advanced usage and API details, refer to the Crawl4AI API documentation.

* * *

---

# Json-CSS Extractor Basic - Crawl4AI Documentation

JSON CSS Extraction Strategy with AsyncWebCrawler
=================================================

The `JsonCssExtractionStrategy` is a powerful feature of Crawl4AI that allows you to extract structured data from web pages using CSS selectors. This method is particularly useful when you need to extract specific data points from a consistent HTML structure, such as tables or repeated elements. Here's how to use it with the AsyncWebCrawler.

Overview
--------

The `JsonCssExtractionStrategy` works by defining a schema that specifies: 1. A base CSS selector for the repeating elements 2. Fields to extract from each element, each with its own CSS selector

This strategy is fast and efficient, as it doesn't rely on external services like LLMs for extraction.

Example: Extracting Cryptocurrency Prices from Coinbase
-------------------------------------------------------

Let's look at an example that extracts cryptocurrency prices from the Coinbase explore page.

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) import json [](#__codelineno-0-2) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-3) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-0-4) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-0-5) [](#__codelineno-0-6) async def extract_structured_data_using_css_extractor(): [](#__codelineno-0-7)     print("\n--- Using JsonCssExtractionStrategy for Fast Structured Output ---") [](#__codelineno-0-8) [](#__codelineno-0-9)     # Define the extraction schema [](#__codelineno-0-10)     schema = { [](#__codelineno-0-11)         "name": "Coinbase Crypto Prices", [](#__codelineno-0-12)         "baseSelector": ".cds-tableRow-t45thuk", [](#__codelineno-0-13)         "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-0-14)             { [](#__codelineno-0-15)                 "name": "crypto", [](#__codelineno-0-16)                 "selector": "td:nth-child(1) h2", [](#__codelineno-0-17)                 "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-0-18)             }, [](#__codelineno-0-19)             { [](#__codelineno-0-20)                 "name": "symbol", [](#__codelineno-0-21)                 "selector": "td:nth-child(1) p", [](#__codelineno-0-22)                 "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-0-23)             }, [](#__codelineno-0-24)             { [](#__codelineno-0-25)                 "name": "price", [](#__codelineno-0-26)                 "selector": "td:nth-child(2)", [](#__codelineno-0-27)                 "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-0-28)             } [](#__codelineno-0-29)         ], [](#__codelineno-0-30)     } [](#__codelineno-0-31) [](#__codelineno-0-32)     # Create the extraction strategy [](#__codelineno-0-33)     extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema, verbose=True) [](#__codelineno-0-34) [](#__codelineno-0-35)     # Use the AsyncWebCrawler with the extraction strategy [](#__codelineno-0-36)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-37)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-38)             url="https://www.coinbase.com/explore", [](#__codelineno-0-39)             extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-0-40)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-0-41)         ) [](#__codelineno-0-42) [](#__codelineno-0-43)         assert result.success, "Failed to crawl the page" [](#__codelineno-0-44) [](#__codelineno-0-45)         # Parse the extracted content [](#__codelineno-0-46)         crypto_prices = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-0-47)         print(f"Successfully extracted {len(crypto_prices)} cryptocurrency prices") [](#__codelineno-0-48)         print(json.dumps(crypto_prices[0], indent=2)) [](#__codelineno-0-49) [](#__codelineno-0-50)     return crypto_prices [](#__codelineno-0-51) [](#__codelineno-0-52) # Run the async function [](#__codelineno-0-53) asyncio.run(extract_structured_data_using_css_extractor())`

Explanation of the Schema
-------------------------

The schema defines how to extract the data:

*   `name`: A descriptive name for the extraction task.
*   `baseSelector`: The CSS selector for the repeating elements (in this case, table rows).
*   `fields`: An array of fields to extract from each element:
*   `name`: The name to give the extracted data.
*   `selector`: The CSS selector to find the specific data within the base element.
*   `type`: The type of data to extract (usually "text" for textual content).

Advantages of JsonCssExtractionStrategy
---------------------------------------

1.  **Speed**: CSS selectors are fast to execute, making this method efficient for large datasets.
2.  **Precision**: You can target exactly the elements you need.
3.  **Structured Output**: The result is already structured as JSON, ready for further processing.
4.  **No External Dependencies**: Unlike LLM-based strategies, this doesn't require any API calls to external services.

Tips for Using JsonCssExtractionStrategy
----------------------------------------

1.  **Inspect the Page**: Use browser developer tools to identify the correct CSS selectors.
2.  **Test Selectors**: Verify your selectors in the browser console before using them in the script.
3.  **Handle Dynamic Content**: If the page uses JavaScript to load content, you may need to combine this with JS execution (see the Advanced Usage section).
4.  **Error Handling**: Always check the `result.success` flag and handle potential failures.

Advanced Usage: Combining with JavaScript Execution
---------------------------------------------------

For pages that load data dynamically, you can combine the `JsonCssExtractionStrategy` with JavaScript execution:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) async def extract_dynamic_structured_data(): [](#__codelineno-1-2)     schema = { [](#__codelineno-1-3)         "name": "Dynamic Crypto Prices", [](#__codelineno-1-4)         "baseSelector": ".crypto-row", [](#__codelineno-1-5)         "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-6)             {"name": "name", "selector": ".crypto-name", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-1-7)             {"name": "price", "selector": ".crypto-price", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-1-8)         ] [](#__codelineno-1-9)     } [](#__codelineno-1-10) [](#__codelineno-1-11)     js_code = """ [](#__codelineno-1-12)     window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight); [](#__codelineno-1-13)     await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 2000));  // Wait for 2 seconds [](#__codelineno-1-14)     """ [](#__codelineno-1-15) [](#__codelineno-1-16)     extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema, verbose=True) [](#__codelineno-1-17) [](#__codelineno-1-18)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-19)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-20)             url="https://example.com/crypto-prices", [](#__codelineno-1-21)             extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-1-22)             js_code=js_code, [](#__codelineno-1-23)             wait_for=".crypto-row:nth-child(20)",  # Wait for 20 rows to load [](#__codelineno-1-24)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-1-25)         ) [](#__codelineno-1-26) [](#__codelineno-1-27)         crypto_data = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-1-28)         print(f"Extracted {len(crypto_data)} cryptocurrency entries") [](#__codelineno-1-29) [](#__codelineno-1-30) asyncio.run(extract_dynamic_structured_data())`

This advanced example demonstrates how to: 1. Execute JavaScript to trigger dynamic content loading. 2. Wait for a specific condition (20 rows loaded) before extraction. 3. Extract data from the dynamically loaded content.

By mastering the `JsonCssExtractionStrategy`, you can efficiently extract structured data from a wide variety of web pages, making it a valuable tool in your web scraping toolkit.

For more details on schema definitions and advanced extraction strategies, check out the[Advanced JsonCssExtraction](../css-advanced/)
.
