# Overview - Crawl4AI Documentation

Extraction Strategies Overview
==============================

Crawl4AI provides powerful extraction strategies to help you get structured data from web pages. Each strategy is designed for specific use cases and offers different approaches to data extraction.

Available Strategies
--------------------

### [LLM-Based Extraction](../llm/)

`LLMExtractionStrategy` uses Language Models to extract structured data from web content. This approach is highly flexible and can understand content semantically.

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) from pydantic import BaseModel [](#__codelineno-0-2) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) class Product(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-0-5)     name: str [](#__codelineno-0-6)     price: float [](#__codelineno-0-7)     description: str [](#__codelineno-0-8) [](#__codelineno-0-9) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-0-10)     provider="ollama/llama2", [](#__codelineno-0-11)     schema=Product.schema(), [](#__codelineno-0-12)     instruction="Extract product details from the page" [](#__codelineno-0-13) ) [](#__codelineno-0-14) [](#__codelineno-0-15) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-16)     url="https://example.com/product", [](#__codelineno-0-17)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-0-18) )`

**Best for:** - Complex data structures - Content requiring interpretation - Flexible content formats - Natural language processing

### [CSS-Based Extraction](../css/)

`JsonCssExtractionStrategy` extracts data using CSS selectors. This is fast, reliable, and perfect for consistently structured pages.

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-1-2) [](#__codelineno-1-3) schema = { [](#__codelineno-1-4)     "name": "Product Listing", [](#__codelineno-1-5)     "baseSelector": ".product-card", [](#__codelineno-1-6)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-7)         {"name": "title", "selector": "h2", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-1-8)         {"name": "price", "selector": ".price", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-1-9)         {"name": "image", "selector": "img", "type": "attribute", "attribute": "src"} [](#__codelineno-1-10)     ] [](#__codelineno-1-11) } [](#__codelineno-1-12) [](#__codelineno-1-13) strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema) [](#__codelineno-1-14) [](#__codelineno-1-15) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-16)     url="https://example.com/products", [](#__codelineno-1-17)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-1-18) )`

**Best for:** - E-commerce product listings - News article collections - Structured content pages - High-performance needs

### [Cosine Strategy](../cosine/)

`CosineStrategy` uses similarity-based clustering to identify and extract relevant content sections.

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import CosineStrategy [](#__codelineno-2-2) [](#__codelineno-2-3) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-2-4)     semantic_filter="product reviews",    # Content focus [](#__codelineno-2-5)     word_count_threshold=10,             # Minimum words per cluster [](#__codelineno-2-6)     sim_threshold=0.3,                   # Similarity threshold [](#__codelineno-2-7)     max_dist=0.2,                        # Maximum cluster distance [](#__codelineno-2-8)     top_k=3                             # Number of top clusters to extract [](#__codelineno-2-9) ) [](#__codelineno-2-10) [](#__codelineno-2-11) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-12)     url="https://example.com/reviews", [](#__codelineno-2-13)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-2-14) )`

**Best for:** - Content similarity analysis - Topic clustering - Relevant content extraction - Pattern recognition in text

Strategy Selection Guide
------------------------

Choose your strategy based on these factors:

1.  **Content Structure**
2.  Well-structured HTML → Use CSS Strategy
3.  Natural language text → Use LLM Strategy
4.  Mixed/Complex content → Use Cosine Strategy
    
5.  **Performance Requirements**
    
6.  Fastest: CSS Strategy
7.  Moderate: Cosine Strategy
8.  Variable: LLM Strategy (depends on provider)
    
9.  **Accuracy Needs**
    
10.  Highest structure accuracy: CSS Strategy
11.  Best semantic understanding: LLM Strategy
12.  Best content relevance: Cosine Strategy

Combining Strategies
--------------------

You can combine strategies for more powerful extraction:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) # First use CSS strategy for initial structure [](#__codelineno-3-2) css_result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-3)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     extraction_strategy=css_strategy [](#__codelineno-3-5) ) [](#__codelineno-3-6) [](#__codelineno-3-7) # Then use LLM for semantic analysis [](#__codelineno-3-8) llm_result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-9)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-3-10)     extraction_strategy=llm_strategy [](#__codelineno-3-11) )`

Common Use Cases
----------------

1.  **E-commerce Scraping**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) # CSS Strategy for product listings [](#__codelineno-4-2) schema = { [](#__codelineno-4-3)     "name": "Products", [](#__codelineno-4-4)     "baseSelector": ".product", [](#__codelineno-4-5)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-4-6)         {"name": "name", "selector": ".title", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-4-7)         {"name": "price", "selector": ".price", "type": "text"} [](#__codelineno-4-8)     ] [](#__codelineno-4-9) }`
    
2.  **News Article Extraction**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-5-1) # LLM Strategy for article content [](#__codelineno-5-2) class Article(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-5-3)     title: str [](#__codelineno-5-4)     content: str [](#__codelineno-5-5)     author: str [](#__codelineno-5-6)     date: str [](#__codelineno-5-7) [](#__codelineno-5-8) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-5-9)     provider="ollama/llama2", [](#__codelineno-5-10)     schema=Article.schema() [](#__codelineno-5-11) )`
    
3.  **Content Analysis**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-6-1) # Cosine Strategy for topic analysis [](#__codelineno-6-2) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-6-3)     semantic_filter="technology trends", [](#__codelineno-6-4)     top_k=5 [](#__codelineno-6-5) )`
    

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Choose the Right Strategy**
2.  Start with CSS for structured data
3.  Use LLM for complex interpretation
4.  Try Cosine for content relevance
    
5.  **Optimize Performance**
    
6.  Cache LLM results
7.  Keep CSS selectors specific
8.  Tune similarity thresholds
    
9.  **Handle Errors**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-7-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-7-3)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-7-4) ) [](#__codelineno-7-5) [](#__codelineno-7-6) if not result.success: [](#__codelineno-7-7)     print(f"Extraction failed: {result.error_message}") [](#__codelineno-7-8) else: [](#__codelineno-7-9)     data = json.loads(result.extracted_content)`
    

Each strategy has its strengths and optimal use cases. Explore the detailed documentation for each strategy to learn more about their specific features and configurations.

* * *

---

# Json-CSS Extractor Advanced - Crawl4AI Documentation

Advanced Usage of JsonCssExtractionStrategy
===========================================

While the basic usage of JsonCssExtractionStrategy is powerful for simple structures, its true potential shines when dealing with complex, nested HTML structures. This section will explore advanced usage scenarios, demonstrating how to extract nested objects, lists, and nested lists.

Hypothetical Website Example
----------------------------

Let's consider a hypothetical e-commerce website that displays product categories, each containing multiple products. Each product has details, reviews, and related items. This complex structure will allow us to demonstrate various advanced features of JsonCssExtractionStrategy.

Assume the HTML structure looks something like this:

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) <div class="category"> [](#__codelineno-0-2)   <h2 class="category-name">Electronics</h2> [](#__codelineno-0-3)   <div class="product"> [](#__codelineno-0-4)     <h3 class="product-name">Smartphone X</h3> [](#__codelineno-0-5)     <p class="product-price">$999</p> [](#__codelineno-0-6)     <div class="product-details"> [](#__codelineno-0-7)       <span class="brand">TechCorp</span> [](#__codelineno-0-8)       <span class="model">X-2000</span> [](#__codelineno-0-9)     </div> [](#__codelineno-0-10)     <ul class="product-features"> [](#__codelineno-0-11)       <li>5G capable</li> [](#__codelineno-0-12)       <li>6.5" OLED screen</li> [](#__codelineno-0-13)       <li>128GB storage</li> [](#__codelineno-0-14)     </ul> [](#__codelineno-0-15)     <div class="product-reviews"> [](#__codelineno-0-16)       <div class="review"> [](#__codelineno-0-17)         <span class="reviewer">John D.</span> [](#__codelineno-0-18)         <span class="rating">4.5</span> [](#__codelineno-0-19)         <p class="review-text">Great phone, love the camera!</p> [](#__codelineno-0-20)       </div> [](#__codelineno-0-21)       <div class="review"> [](#__codelineno-0-22)         <span class="reviewer">Jane S.</span> [](#__codelineno-0-23)         <span class="rating">5</span> [](#__codelineno-0-24)         <p class="review-text">Best smartphone I've ever owned.</p> [](#__codelineno-0-25)       </div> [](#__codelineno-0-26)     </div> [](#__codelineno-0-27)     <ul class="related-products"> [](#__codelineno-0-28)       <li> [](#__codelineno-0-29)         <span class="related-name">Phone Case</span> [](#__codelineno-0-30)         <span class="related-price">$29.99</span> [](#__codelineno-0-31)       </li> [](#__codelineno-0-32)       <li> [](#__codelineno-0-33)         <span class="related-name">Screen Protector</span> [](#__codelineno-0-34)         <span class="related-price">$9.99</span> [](#__codelineno-0-35)       </li> [](#__codelineno-0-36)     </ul> [](#__codelineno-0-37)   </div> [](#__codelineno-0-38)   <!-- More products... --> [](#__codelineno-0-39) </div>`

Now, let's create a schema to extract this complex structure:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) schema = { [](#__codelineno-1-2)     "name": "E-commerce Product Catalog", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     "baseSelector": "div.category", [](#__codelineno-1-4)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-5)         { [](#__codelineno-1-6)             "name": "category_name", [](#__codelineno-1-7)             "selector": "h2.category-name", [](#__codelineno-1-8)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-9)         }, [](#__codelineno-1-10)         { [](#__codelineno-1-11)             "name": "products", [](#__codelineno-1-12)             "selector": "div.product", [](#__codelineno-1-13)             "type": "nested_list", [](#__codelineno-1-14)             "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-15)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-16)                     "name": "name", [](#__codelineno-1-17)                     "selector": "h3.product-name", [](#__codelineno-1-18)                     "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-19)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-20)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-21)                     "name": "price", [](#__codelineno-1-22)                     "selector": "p.product-price", [](#__codelineno-1-23)                     "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-24)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-25)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-26)                     "name": "details", [](#__codelineno-1-27)                     "selector": "div.product-details", [](#__codelineno-1-28)                     "type": "nested", [](#__codelineno-1-29)                     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-30)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-31)                             "name": "brand", [](#__codelineno-1-32)                             "selector": "span.brand", [](#__codelineno-1-33)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-34)                         }, [](#__codelineno-1-35)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-36)                             "name": "model", [](#__codelineno-1-37)                             "selector": "span.model", [](#__codelineno-1-38)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-39)                         } [](#__codelineno-1-40)                     ] [](#__codelineno-1-41)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-42)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-43)                     "name": "features", [](#__codelineno-1-44)                     "selector": "ul.product-features li", [](#__codelineno-1-45)                     "type": "list", [](#__codelineno-1-46)                     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-47)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-48)                             "name": "feature", [](#__codelineno-1-49)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-50)                         } [](#__codelineno-1-51)                     ] [](#__codelineno-1-52)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-53)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-54)                     "name": "reviews", [](#__codelineno-1-55)                     "selector": "div.review", [](#__codelineno-1-56)                     "type": "nested_list", [](#__codelineno-1-57)                     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-58)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-59)                             "name": "reviewer", [](#__codelineno-1-60)                             "selector": "span.reviewer", [](#__codelineno-1-61)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-62)                         }, [](#__codelineno-1-63)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-64)                             "name": "rating", [](#__codelineno-1-65)                             "selector": "span.rating", [](#__codelineno-1-66)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-67)                         }, [](#__codelineno-1-68)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-69)                             "name": "comment", [](#__codelineno-1-70)                             "selector": "p.review-text", [](#__codelineno-1-71)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-72)                         } [](#__codelineno-1-73)                     ] [](#__codelineno-1-74)                 }, [](#__codelineno-1-75)                 { [](#__codelineno-1-76)                     "name": "related_products", [](#__codelineno-1-77)                     "selector": "ul.related-products li", [](#__codelineno-1-78)                     "type": "list", [](#__codelineno-1-79)                     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-1-80)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-81)                             "name": "name", [](#__codelineno-1-82)                             "selector": "span.related-name", [](#__codelineno-1-83)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-84)                         }, [](#__codelineno-1-85)                         { [](#__codelineno-1-86)                             "name": "price", [](#__codelineno-1-87)                             "selector": "span.related-price", [](#__codelineno-1-88)                             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-1-89)                         } [](#__codelineno-1-90)                     ] [](#__codelineno-1-91)                 } [](#__codelineno-1-92)             ] [](#__codelineno-1-93)         } [](#__codelineno-1-94)     ] [](#__codelineno-1-95) }`

This schema demonstrates several advanced features:

1.  **Nested Objects**: The `details` field is a nested object within each product.
2.  **Simple Lists**: The `features` field is a simple list of text items.
3.  **Nested Lists**: The `products` field is a nested list, where each item is a complex object.
4.  **Lists of Objects**: The `reviews` and `related_products` fields are lists of objects.

Let's break down the key concepts:

### Nested Objects

To create a nested object, use `"type": "nested"` and provide a `fields` array for the nested structure:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) { [](#__codelineno-2-2)     "name": "details", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     "selector": "div.product-details", [](#__codelineno-2-4)     "type": "nested", [](#__codelineno-2-5)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-2-6)         { [](#__codelineno-2-7)             "name": "brand", [](#__codelineno-2-8)             "selector": "span.brand", [](#__codelineno-2-9)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-2-10)         }, [](#__codelineno-2-11)         { [](#__codelineno-2-12)             "name": "model", [](#__codelineno-2-13)             "selector": "span.model", [](#__codelineno-2-14)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-2-15)         } [](#__codelineno-2-16)     ] [](#__codelineno-2-17) }`

### Simple Lists

For a simple list of identical items, use `"type": "list"`:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) { [](#__codelineno-3-2)     "name": "features", [](#__codelineno-3-3)     "selector": "ul.product-features li", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     "type": "list", [](#__codelineno-3-5)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-3-6)         { [](#__codelineno-3-7)             "name": "feature", [](#__codelineno-3-8)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-3-9)         } [](#__codelineno-3-10)     ] [](#__codelineno-3-11) }`

### Nested Lists

For a list of complex objects, use `"type": "nested_list"`:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) { [](#__codelineno-4-2)     "name": "products", [](#__codelineno-4-3)     "selector": "div.product", [](#__codelineno-4-4)     "type": "nested_list", [](#__codelineno-4-5)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-4-6)         // ... fields for each product [](#__codelineno-4-7)     ] [](#__codelineno-4-8) }`

### Lists of Objects

Similar to nested lists, but typically used for simpler objects within the list:

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) { [](#__codelineno-5-2)     "name": "related_products", [](#__codelineno-5-3)     "selector": "ul.related-products li", [](#__codelineno-5-4)     "type": "list", [](#__codelineno-5-5)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-5-6)         { [](#__codelineno-5-7)             "name": "name", [](#__codelineno-5-8)             "selector": "span.related-name", [](#__codelineno-5-9)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-5-10)         }, [](#__codelineno-5-11)         { [](#__codelineno-5-12)             "name": "price", [](#__codelineno-5-13)             "selector": "span.related-price", [](#__codelineno-5-14)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-5-15)         } [](#__codelineno-5-16)     ] [](#__codelineno-5-17) }`

Using the Advanced Schema
-------------------------

To use this advanced schema with AsyncWebCrawler:

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) import json [](#__codelineno-6-2) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-6-3) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-6-4) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-6-5) [](#__codelineno-6-6) async def extract_complex_product_data(): [](#__codelineno-6-7)     extraction_strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema, verbose=True) [](#__codelineno-6-8) [](#__codelineno-6-9)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-6-10)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-6-11)             url="https://gist.githubusercontent.com/githubusercontent/2d7b8ba3cd8ab6cf3c8da771ddb36878/raw/1ae2f90c6861ce7dd84cc50d3df9920dee5e1fd2/sample_ecommerce.html", [](#__codelineno-6-12)             extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-6-13)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-6-14)         ) [](#__codelineno-6-15) [](#__codelineno-6-16)         assert result.success, "Failed to crawl the page" [](#__codelineno-6-17) [](#__codelineno-6-18)         product_data = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-6-19)         print(json.dumps(product_data, indent=2)) [](#__codelineno-6-20) [](#__codelineno-6-21) asyncio.run(extract_complex_product_data())`

This will produce a structured JSON output that captures the complex hierarchy of the product catalog, including nested objects, lists, and nested lists.

Tips for Advanced Usage
-----------------------

1.  **Start Simple**: Begin with a basic schema and gradually add complexity.
2.  **Test Incrementally**: Test each part of your schema separately before combining them.
3.  **Use Chrome DevTools**: The Element Inspector is invaluable for identifying the correct selectors.
4.  **Handle Missing Data**: Use the `default` key in your field definitions to handle cases where data might be missing.
5.  **Leverage Transforms**: Use the `transform` key to clean or format extracted data (e.g., converting prices to numbers).
6.  **Consider Performance**: Very complex schemas might slow down extraction. Balance complexity with performance needs.

By mastering these advanced techniques, you can use JsonCssExtractionStrategy to extract highly structured data from even the most complex web pages, making it a powerful tool for web scraping and data analysis tasks.

# Page Interaction - Crawl4AI Documentation

Page Interaction
================

Crawl4AI provides powerful features for interacting with dynamic webpages, handling JavaScript execution, and managing page events.

JavaScript Execution
--------------------

### Basic Execution

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) # Single JavaScript command [](#__codelineno-0-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-3)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-4)     js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);" [](#__codelineno-0-5) ) [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Multiple commands [](#__codelineno-0-8) js_commands = [ [](#__codelineno-0-9)     "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-0-10)     "document.querySelector('.load-more').click();", [](#__codelineno-0-11)     "document.querySelector('#consent-button').click();" [](#__codelineno-0-12) ] [](#__codelineno-0-13) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-14)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-15)     js_code=js_commands [](#__codelineno-0-16) )`

Wait Conditions
---------------

### CSS-Based Waiting

Wait for elements to appear:

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     wait_for="css:.dynamic-content"  # Wait for element with class 'dynamic-content' [](#__codelineno-1-4) )`

### JavaScript-Based Waiting

Wait for custom conditions:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) # Wait for number of elements [](#__codelineno-2-2) wait_condition = """() => { [](#__codelineno-2-3)     return document.querySelectorAll('.item').length > 10; [](#__codelineno-2-4) }""" [](#__codelineno-2-5) [](#__codelineno-2-6) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-7)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-8)     wait_for=f"js:{wait_condition}" [](#__codelineno-2-9) ) [](#__codelineno-2-10) [](#__codelineno-2-11) # Wait for dynamic content to load [](#__codelineno-2-12) wait_for_content = """() => { [](#__codelineno-2-13)     const content = document.querySelector('.content'); [](#__codelineno-2-14)     return content && content.innerText.length > 100; [](#__codelineno-2-15) }""" [](#__codelineno-2-16) [](#__codelineno-2-17) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-18)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-19)     wait_for=f"js:{wait_for_content}" [](#__codelineno-2-20) )`

Handling Dynamic Content
------------------------

### Load More Content

Handle infinite scroll or load more buttons:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) # Scroll and wait pattern [](#__codelineno-3-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-3)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     js_code=[ [](#__codelineno-3-5)         # Scroll to bottom [](#__codelineno-3-6)         "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-3-7)         # Click load more if exists [](#__codelineno-3-8)         "const loadMore = document.querySelector('.load-more'); if(loadMore) loadMore.click();" [](#__codelineno-3-9)     ], [](#__codelineno-3-10)     # Wait for new content [](#__codelineno-3-11)     wait_for="js:() => document.querySelectorAll('.item').length > previousCount" [](#__codelineno-3-12) )`

### Form Interaction

Handle forms and inputs:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) js_form_interaction = """ [](#__codelineno-4-2)     // Fill form fields [](#__codelineno-4-3)     document.querySelector('#search').value = 'search term'; [](#__codelineno-4-4)     // Submit form [](#__codelineno-4-5)     document.querySelector('form').submit(); [](#__codelineno-4-6) """ [](#__codelineno-4-7) [](#__codelineno-4-8) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-9)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-10)     js_code=js_form_interaction, [](#__codelineno-4-11)     wait_for="css:.results"  # Wait for results to load [](#__codelineno-4-12) )`

Timing Control
--------------

### Delays and Timeouts

Control timing of interactions:

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-5-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-5-3)     page_timeout=60000,              # Page load timeout (ms) [](#__codelineno-5-4)     delay_before_return_html=2.0,    # Wait before capturing content [](#__codelineno-5-5) )`

Complex Interactions Example
----------------------------

Here's an example of handling a dynamic page with multiple interactions:

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) async def crawl_dynamic_content(): [](#__codelineno-6-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-6-3)         # Initial page load [](#__codelineno-6-4)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-6-5)             url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-6-6)             # Handle cookie consent [](#__codelineno-6-7)             js_code="document.querySelector('.cookie-accept')?.click();", [](#__codelineno-6-8)             wait_for="css:.main-content" [](#__codelineno-6-9)         ) [](#__codelineno-6-10) [](#__codelineno-6-11)         # Load more content [](#__codelineno-6-12)         session_id = "dynamic_session"  # Keep session for multiple interactions [](#__codelineno-6-13) [](#__codelineno-6-14)         for page in range(3):  # Load 3 pages of content [](#__codelineno-6-15)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-6-16)                 url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-6-17)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-6-18)                 js_code=[ [](#__codelineno-6-19)                     # Scroll to bottom [](#__codelineno-6-20)                     "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-6-21)                     # Store current item count [](#__codelineno-6-22)                     "window.previousCount = document.querySelectorAll('.item').length;", [](#__codelineno-6-23)                     # Click load more [](#__codelineno-6-24)                     "document.querySelector('.load-more')?.click();" [](#__codelineno-6-25)                 ], [](#__codelineno-6-26)                 # Wait for new items [](#__codelineno-6-27)                 wait_for="""() => { [](#__codelineno-6-28)                     const currentCount = document.querySelectorAll('.item').length; [](#__codelineno-6-29)                     return currentCount > window.previousCount; [](#__codelineno-6-30)                 }""", [](#__codelineno-6-31)                 # Only execute JS without reloading page [](#__codelineno-6-32)                 js_only=True if page > 0 else False [](#__codelineno-6-33)             ) [](#__codelineno-6-34) [](#__codelineno-6-35)             # Process content after each load [](#__codelineno-6-36)             print(f"Page {page + 1} items:", len(result.cleaned_html)) [](#__codelineno-6-37) [](#__codelineno-6-38)         # Clean up session [](#__codelineno-6-39)         await crawler.crawler_strategy.kill_session(session_id)`

Using with Extraction Strategies
--------------------------------

Combine page interaction with structured extraction:

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy, LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-7-2) [](#__codelineno-7-3) # Pattern-based extraction after interaction [](#__codelineno-7-4) schema = { [](#__codelineno-7-5)     "name": "Dynamic Items", [](#__codelineno-7-6)     "baseSelector": ".item", [](#__codelineno-7-7)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-7-8)         {"name": "title", "selector": "h2", "type": "text"}, [](#__codelineno-7-9)         {"name": "description", "selector": ".desc", "type": "text"} [](#__codelineno-7-10)     ] [](#__codelineno-7-11) } [](#__codelineno-7-12) [](#__codelineno-7-13) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-14)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-7-15)     js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-7-16)     wait_for="css:.item:nth-child(10)",  # Wait for 10 items [](#__codelineno-7-17)     extraction_strategy=JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema) [](#__codelineno-7-18) ) [](#__codelineno-7-19) [](#__codelineno-7-20) # Or use LLM to analyze dynamic content [](#__codelineno-7-21) class ContentAnalysis(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-7-22)     topics: List[str] [](#__codelineno-7-23)     summary: str [](#__codelineno-7-24) [](#__codelineno-7-25) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-26)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-7-27)     js_code="document.querySelector('.show-more').click();", [](#__codelineno-7-28)     wait_for="css:.full-content", [](#__codelineno-7-29)     extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-7-30)         provider="ollama/nemotron", [](#__codelineno-7-31)         schema=ContentAnalysis.schema(), [](#__codelineno-7-32)         instruction="Analyze the full content" [](#__codelineno-7-33)     ) [](#__codelineno-7-34) )`

# Chunking - Crawl4AI Documentation

Chunking Strategies 📚
----------------------

Crawl4AI provides several powerful chunking strategies to divide text into manageable parts for further processing. Each strategy has unique characteristics and is suitable for different scenarios. Let's explore them one by one.

### RegexChunking

`RegexChunking` splits text using regular expressions. This is ideal for creating chunks based on specific patterns like paragraphs or sentences.

#### When to Use

*   Great for structured text with consistent delimiters.
*   Suitable for documents where specific patterns (e.g., double newlines, periods) indicate logical chunks.

#### Parameters

*   `patterns` (list, optional): Regular expressions used to split the text. Default is to split by double newlines (`['\n\n']`).

#### Example

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import RegexChunking [](#__codelineno-0-2) [](#__codelineno-0-3) # Define patterns for splitting text [](#__codelineno-0-4) patterns = [r'\n\n', r'\. '] [](#__codelineno-0-5) chunker = RegexChunking(patterns=patterns) [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Sample text [](#__codelineno-0-8) text = "This is a sample text. It will be split into chunks.\n\nThis is another paragraph." [](#__codelineno-0-9) [](#__codelineno-0-10) # Chunk the text [](#__codelineno-0-11) chunks = chunker.chunk(text) [](#__codelineno-0-12) print(chunks)`

### NlpSentenceChunking

`NlpSentenceChunking` uses NLP models to split text into sentences, ensuring accurate sentence boundaries.

#### When to Use

*   Ideal for texts where sentence boundaries are crucial.
*   Useful for creating chunks that preserve grammatical structures.

#### Parameters

*   None.

#### Example

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import NlpSentenceChunking [](#__codelineno-1-2) [](#__codelineno-1-3) chunker = NlpSentenceChunking() [](#__codelineno-1-4) [](#__codelineno-1-5) # Sample text [](#__codelineno-1-6) text = "This is a sample text. It will be split into sentences. Here's another sentence." [](#__codelineno-1-7) [](#__codelineno-1-8) # Chunk the text [](#__codelineno-1-9) chunks = chunker.chunk(text) [](#__codelineno-1-10) print(chunks)`

### TopicSegmentationChunking

`TopicSegmentationChunking` employs the TextTiling algorithm to segment text into topic-based chunks. This method identifies thematic boundaries.

#### When to Use

*   Perfect for long documents with distinct topics.
*   Useful when preserving topic continuity is more important than maintaining text order.

#### Parameters

*   `num_keywords` (int, optional): Number of keywords for each topic segment. Default is `3`.

#### Example

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import TopicSegmentationChunking [](#__codelineno-2-2) [](#__codelineno-2-3) chunker = TopicSegmentationChunking(num_keywords=3) [](#__codelineno-2-4) [](#__codelineno-2-5) # Sample text [](#__codelineno-2-6) text = "This document contains several topics. Topic one discusses AI. Topic two covers machine learning." [](#__codelineno-2-7) [](#__codelineno-2-8) # Chunk the text [](#__codelineno-2-9) chunks = chunker.chunk(text) [](#__codelineno-2-10) print(chunks)`

### FixedLengthWordChunking

`FixedLengthWordChunking` splits text into chunks based on a fixed number of words. This ensures each chunk has approximately the same length.

#### When to Use

*   Suitable for processing large texts where uniform chunk size is important.
*   Useful when the number of words per chunk needs to be controlled.

#### Parameters

*   `chunk_size` (int, optional): Number of words per chunk. Default is `100`.

#### Example

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import FixedLengthWordChunking [](#__codelineno-3-2) [](#__codelineno-3-3) chunker = FixedLengthWordChunking(chunk_size=10) [](#__codelineno-3-4) [](#__codelineno-3-5) # Sample text [](#__codelineno-3-6) text = "This is a sample text. It will be split into chunks of fixed length." [](#__codelineno-3-7) [](#__codelineno-3-8) # Chunk the text [](#__codelineno-3-9) chunks = chunker.chunk(text) [](#__codelineno-3-10) print(chunks)`

### SlidingWindowChunking

`SlidingWindowChunking` uses a sliding window approach to create overlapping chunks. Each chunk has a fixed length, and the window slides by a specified step size.

#### When to Use

*   Ideal for creating overlapping chunks to preserve context.
*   Useful for tasks where context from adjacent chunks is needed.

#### Parameters

*   `window_size` (int, optional): Number of words in each chunk. Default is `100`.
*   `step` (int, optional): Number of words to slide the window. Default is `50`.

#### Example

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import SlidingWindowChunking [](#__codelineno-4-2) [](#__codelineno-4-3) chunker = SlidingWindowChunking(window_size=10, step=5) [](#__codelineno-4-4) [](#__codelineno-4-5) # Sample text [](#__codelineno-4-6) text = "This is a sample text. It will be split using a sliding window approach to preserve context." [](#__codelineno-4-7) [](#__codelineno-4-8) # Chunk the text [](#__codelineno-4-9) chunks = chunker.chunk(text) [](#__codelineno-4-10) print(chunks)`

With these chunking strategies, you can choose the best method to divide your text based on your specific needs. Whether you need precise sentence boundaries, topic-based segmentation, or uniform chunk sizes, Crawl4AI has you covered. Happy chunking! 📝✨

* * *

# LLM Strategy - Crawl4AI Documentation

LLM Extraction with AsyncWebCrawler
===================================

Crawl4AI's AsyncWebCrawler allows you to use Language Models (LLMs) to extract structured data or relevant content from web pages asynchronously. Below are two examples demonstrating how to use `LLMExtractionStrategy` for different purposes with the AsyncWebCrawler.

Example 1: Extract Structured Data
----------------------------------

In this example, we use the `LLMExtractionStrategy` to extract structured data (model names and their fees) from the OpenAI pricing page.

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) import os [](#__codelineno-0-2) import json [](#__codelineno-0-3) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-4) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-0-5) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-0-6) from pydantic import BaseModel, Field [](#__codelineno-0-7) [](#__codelineno-0-8) class OpenAIModelFee(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-0-9)     model_name: str = Field(..., description="Name of the OpenAI model.") [](#__codelineno-0-10)     input_fee: str = Field(..., description="Fee for input token for the OpenAI model.") [](#__codelineno-0-11)     output_fee: str = Field(..., description="Fee for output token for the OpenAI model.") [](#__codelineno-0-12) [](#__codelineno-0-13) async def extract_openai_fees(): [](#__codelineno-0-14)     url = 'https://openai.com/api/pricing/' [](#__codelineno-0-15) [](#__codelineno-0-16)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-17)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-18)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-0-19)             word_count_threshold=1, [](#__codelineno-0-20)             extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-0-21)                 provider="openai/gpt-4o", # Or use ollama like provider="ollama/nemotron" [](#__codelineno-0-22)                 api_token=os.getenv('OPENAI_API_KEY'), [](#__codelineno-0-23)                 schema=OpenAIModelFee.model_json_schema(), [](#__codelineno-0-24)                 extraction_type="schema", [](#__codelineno-0-25)                 instruction="From the crawled content, extract all mentioned model names along with their " [](#__codelineno-0-26)                             "fees for input and output tokens. Make sure not to miss anything in the entire content. " [](#__codelineno-0-27)                             'One extracted model JSON format should look like this: ' [](#__codelineno-0-28)                             '{ "model_name": "GPT-4", "input_fee": "US$10.00 / 1M tokens", "output_fee": "US$30.00 / 1M tokens" }' [](#__codelineno-0-29)             ), [](#__codelineno-0-30)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-0-31)         ) [](#__codelineno-0-32) [](#__codelineno-0-33)     model_fees = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-0-34)     print(f"Number of models extracted: {len(model_fees)}") [](#__codelineno-0-35) [](#__codelineno-0-36)     with open(".data/openai_fees.json", "w", encoding="utf-8") as f: [](#__codelineno-0-37)         json.dump(model_fees, f, indent=2) [](#__codelineno-0-38) [](#__codelineno-0-39) asyncio.run(extract_openai_fees())`

Example 2: Extract Relevant Content
-----------------------------------

In this example, we instruct the LLM to extract only content related to technology from the NBC News business page.

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) import os [](#__codelineno-1-2) import json [](#__codelineno-1-3) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-1-4) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-1-5) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-1-6) [](#__codelineno-1-7) async def extract_tech_content(): [](#__codelineno-1-8)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-9)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-10)             url="https://www.nbcnews.com/business", [](#__codelineno-1-11)             extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-1-12)                 provider="openai/gpt-4o", [](#__codelineno-1-13)                 api_token=os.getenv('OPENAI_API_KEY'), [](#__codelineno-1-14)                 instruction="Extract only content related to technology" [](#__codelineno-1-15)             ), [](#__codelineno-1-16)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-1-17)         ) [](#__codelineno-1-18) [](#__codelineno-1-19)     tech_content = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-1-20)     print(f"Number of tech-related items extracted: {len(tech_content)}") [](#__codelineno-1-21) [](#__codelineno-1-22)     with open(".data/tech_content.json", "w", encoding="utf-8") as f: [](#__codelineno-1-23)         json.dump(tech_content, f, indent=2) [](#__codelineno-1-24) [](#__codelineno-1-25) asyncio.run(extract_tech_content())`

Advanced Usage: Combining JS Execution with LLM Extraction
----------------------------------------------------------

This example demonstrates how to combine JavaScript execution with LLM extraction to handle dynamic content:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def extract_dynamic_content(): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     js_code = """ [](#__codelineno-2-3)     const loadMoreButton = Array.from(document.querySelectorAll('button')).find(button => button.textContent.includes('Load More')); [](#__codelineno-2-4)     if (loadMoreButton) { [](#__codelineno-2-5)         loadMoreButton.click(); [](#__codelineno-2-6)         await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 2000)); [](#__codelineno-2-7)     } [](#__codelineno-2-8)     """ [](#__codelineno-2-9) [](#__codelineno-2-10)     wait_for = """ [](#__codelineno-2-11)     () => { [](#__codelineno-2-12)         const articles = document.querySelectorAll('article.tease-card'); [](#__codelineno-2-13)         return articles.length > 10; [](#__codelineno-2-14)     } [](#__codelineno-2-15)     """ [](#__codelineno-2-16) [](#__codelineno-2-17)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-18)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-19)             url="https://www.nbcnews.com/business", [](#__codelineno-2-20)             js_code=js_code, [](#__codelineno-2-21)             wait_for=wait_for, [](#__codelineno-2-22)             css_selector="article.tease-card", [](#__codelineno-2-23)             extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-2-24)                 provider="openai/gpt-4o", [](#__codelineno-2-25)                 api_token=os.getenv('OPENAI_API_KEY'), [](#__codelineno-2-26)                 instruction="Summarize each article, focusing on technology-related content" [](#__codelineno-2-27)             ), [](#__codelineno-2-28)             bypass_cache=True, [](#__codelineno-2-29)         ) [](#__codelineno-2-30) [](#__codelineno-2-31)     summaries = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-2-32)     print(f"Number of summarized articles: {len(summaries)}") [](#__codelineno-2-33) [](#__codelineno-2-34)     with open(".data/tech_summaries.json", "w", encoding="utf-8") as f: [](#__codelineno-2-35)         json.dump(summaries, f, indent=2) [](#__codelineno-2-36) [](#__codelineno-2-37) asyncio.run(extract_dynamic_content())`

Customizing LLM Provider
------------------------

Crawl4AI uses the `litellm` library under the hood, which allows you to use any LLM provider you want. Just pass the correct model name and API token:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) extraction_strategy=LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-3-2)     provider="your_llm_provider/model_name", [](#__codelineno-3-3)     api_token="your_api_token", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     instruction="Your extraction instruction" [](#__codelineno-3-5) )`

This flexibility allows you to integrate with various LLM providers and tailor the extraction process to your specific needs.

Error Handling and Retries
--------------------------

When working with external LLM APIs, it's important to handle potential errors and implement retry logic. Here's an example of how you might do this:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-4-2) from tenacity import retry, stop_after_attempt, wait_exponential [](#__codelineno-4-3) [](#__codelineno-4-4) class LLMExtractionError(Exception): [](#__codelineno-4-5)     pass [](#__codelineno-4-6) [](#__codelineno-4-7) @retry(stop=stop_after_attempt(3), wait=wait_exponential(multiplier=1, min=4, max=10)) [](#__codelineno-4-8) async def extract_with_retry(crawler, url, extraction_strategy): [](#__codelineno-4-9)     try: [](#__codelineno-4-10)         result = await crawler.arun(url=url, extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, bypass_cache=True) [](#__codelineno-4-11)         return json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-4-12)     except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-4-13)         raise LLMExtractionError(f"Failed to extract content: {str(e)}") [](#__codelineno-4-14) [](#__codelineno-4-15) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-4-16)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-17)         try: [](#__codelineno-4-18)             content = await extract_with_retry( [](#__codelineno-4-19)                 crawler, [](#__codelineno-4-20)                 "https://www.example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-21)                 LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-4-22)                     provider="openai/gpt-4o", [](#__codelineno-4-23)                     api_token=os.getenv('OPENAI_API_KEY'), [](#__codelineno-4-24)                     instruction="Extract and summarize main points" [](#__codelineno-4-25)                 ) [](#__codelineno-4-26)             ) [](#__codelineno-4-27)             print("Extracted content:", content) [](#__codelineno-4-28)         except LLMExtractionError as e: [](#__codelineno-4-29)             print(f"Extraction failed after retries: {e}") [](#__codelineno-4-30) [](#__codelineno-4-31) asyncio.run(main())`

This example uses the `tenacity` library to implement a retry mechanism with exponential backoff, which can help handle temporary failures or rate limiting from the LLM API.

# Cosine Strategy - Crawl4AI Documentation

Cosine Strategy
===============

The Cosine Strategy in Crawl4AI uses similarity-based clustering to identify and extract relevant content sections from web pages. This strategy is particularly useful when you need to find and extract content based on semantic similarity rather than structural patterns.

How It Works
------------

The Cosine Strategy: 1. Breaks down page content into meaningful chunks 2. Converts text into vector representations 3. Calculates similarity between chunks 4. Clusters similar content together 5. Ranks and filters content based on relevance

Basic Usage
-----------

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import CosineStrategy [](#__codelineno-0-2) [](#__codelineno-0-3) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-0-4)     semantic_filter="product reviews",    # Target content type [](#__codelineno-0-5)     word_count_threshold=10,             # Minimum words per cluster [](#__codelineno-0-6)     sim_threshold=0.3                    # Similarity threshold [](#__codelineno-0-7) ) [](#__codelineno-0-8) [](#__codelineno-0-9) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-10)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-11)         url="https://example.com/reviews", [](#__codelineno-0-12)         extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-0-13)     ) [](#__codelineno-0-14) [](#__codelineno-0-15)     content = result.extracted_content`

Configuration Options
---------------------

### Core Parameters

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     # Content Filtering [](#__codelineno-1-3)     semantic_filter: str = None,       # Keywords/topic for content filtering [](#__codelineno-1-4)     word_count_threshold: int = 10,    # Minimum words per cluster [](#__codelineno-1-5)     sim_threshold: float = 0.3,        # Similarity threshold (0.0 to 1.0) [](#__codelineno-1-6) [](#__codelineno-1-7)     # Clustering Parameters [](#__codelineno-1-8)     max_dist: float = 0.2,            # Maximum distance for clustering [](#__codelineno-1-9)     linkage_method: str = 'ward',      # Clustering linkage method [](#__codelineno-1-10)     top_k: int = 3,                   # Number of top categories to extract [](#__codelineno-1-11) [](#__codelineno-1-12)     # Model Configuration [](#__codelineno-1-13)     model_name: str = 'sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2',  # Embedding model [](#__codelineno-1-14) [](#__codelineno-1-15)     verbose: bool = False             # Enable logging [](#__codelineno-1-16) )`

### Parameter Details

1.  **semantic\_filter**
2.  Sets the target topic or content type
3.  Use keywords relevant to your desired content
4.  Example: "technical specifications", "user reviews", "pricing information"
    
5.  **sim\_threshold**
    
6.  Controls how similar content must be to be grouped together
7.  Higher values (e.g., 0.8) mean stricter matching
8.  Lower values (e.g., 0.3) allow more variation
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) # Strict matching [](#__codelineno-2-2) strategy = CosineStrategy(sim_threshold=0.8) [](#__codelineno-2-3) [](#__codelineno-2-4) # Loose matching [](#__codelineno-2-5) strategy = CosineStrategy(sim_threshold=0.3)`
    
9.  **word\_count\_threshold**
    
10.  Filters out short content blocks
11.  Helps eliminate noise and irrelevant content
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) # Only consider substantial paragraphs [](#__codelineno-3-2) strategy = CosineStrategy(word_count_threshold=50)`
    
12.  **top\_k**
    
13.  Number of top content clusters to return
14.  Higher values return more diverse content
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) # Get top 5 most relevant content clusters [](#__codelineno-4-2) strategy = CosineStrategy(top_k=5)`
    

Use Cases
---------

### 1\. Article Content Extraction

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-5-2)     semantic_filter="main article content", [](#__codelineno-5-3)     word_count_threshold=100,  # Longer blocks for articles [](#__codelineno-5-4)     top_k=1                   # Usually want single main content [](#__codelineno-5-5) ) [](#__codelineno-5-6) [](#__codelineno-5-7) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-5-8)     url="https://example.com/blog/post", [](#__codelineno-5-9)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-5-10) )`

### 2\. Product Review Analysis

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-6-2)     semantic_filter="customer reviews and ratings", [](#__codelineno-6-3)     word_count_threshold=20,   # Reviews can be shorter [](#__codelineno-6-4)     top_k=10,                 # Get multiple reviews [](#__codelineno-6-5)     sim_threshold=0.4         # Allow variety in review content [](#__codelineno-6-6) )`

### 3\. Technical Documentation

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-7-2)     semantic_filter="technical specifications documentation", [](#__codelineno-7-3)     word_count_threshold=30, [](#__codelineno-7-4)     sim_threshold=0.6,        # Stricter matching for technical content [](#__codelineno-7-5)     max_dist=0.3             # Allow related technical sections [](#__codelineno-7-6) )`

Advanced Features
-----------------

### Custom Clustering

`[](#__codelineno-8-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-8-2)     linkage_method='complete',  # Alternative clustering method [](#__codelineno-8-3)     max_dist=0.4,              # Larger clusters [](#__codelineno-8-4)     model_name='sentence-transformers/paraphrase-multilingual-MiniLM-L12-v2'  # Multilingual support [](#__codelineno-8-5) )`

### Content Filtering Pipeline

`[](#__codelineno-9-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-9-2)     semantic_filter="pricing plans features", [](#__codelineno-9-3)     word_count_threshold=15, [](#__codelineno-9-4)     sim_threshold=0.5, [](#__codelineno-9-5)     top_k=3 [](#__codelineno-9-6) ) [](#__codelineno-9-7) [](#__codelineno-9-8) async def extract_pricing_features(url: str): [](#__codelineno-9-9)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-9-10)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-9-11)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-9-12)             extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-9-13)         ) [](#__codelineno-9-14) [](#__codelineno-9-15)         if result.success: [](#__codelineno-9-16)             content = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-9-17)             return { [](#__codelineno-9-18)                 'pricing_features': content, [](#__codelineno-9-19)                 'clusters': len(content), [](#__codelineno-9-20)                 'similarity_scores': [item['score'] for item in content] [](#__codelineno-9-21)             }`

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Adjust Thresholds Iteratively**
2.  Start with default values
3.  Adjust based on results
4.  Monitor clustering quality
    
5.  **Choose Appropriate Word Count Thresholds**
    
6.  Higher for articles (100+)
7.  Lower for reviews/comments (20+)
8.  Medium for product descriptions (50+)
    
9.  **Optimize Performance**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-10-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-10-2)     word_count_threshold=10,  # Filter early [](#__codelineno-10-3)     top_k=5,                 # Limit results [](#__codelineno-10-4)     verbose=True             # Monitor performance [](#__codelineno-10-5) )`
    
10.  **Handle Different Content Types**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-11-1) # For mixed content pages [](#__codelineno-11-2) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-11-3)     semantic_filter="product features", [](#__codelineno-11-4)     sim_threshold=0.4,      # More flexible matching [](#__codelineno-11-5)     max_dist=0.3,          # Larger clusters [](#__codelineno-11-6)     top_k=3                # Multiple relevant sections [](#__codelineno-11-7) )`
    

Error Handling
--------------

`[](#__codelineno-12-1) try: [](#__codelineno-12-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-12-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-12-4)         extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-12-5)     ) [](#__codelineno-12-6) [](#__codelineno-12-7)     if result.success: [](#__codelineno-12-8)         content = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-12-9)         if not content: [](#__codelineno-12-10)             print("No relevant content found") [](#__codelineno-12-11)     else: [](#__codelineno-12-12)         print(f"Extraction failed: {result.error_message}") [](#__codelineno-12-13) [](#__codelineno-12-14) except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-12-15)     print(f"Error during extraction: {str(e)}")`

The Cosine Strategy is particularly effective when: - Content structure is inconsistent - You need semantic understanding - You want to find similar content blocks - Structure-based extraction (CSS/XPath) isn't reliable

It works well with other strategies and can be used as a pre-processing step for LLM-based extraction.

* * *

# Strategies - Crawl4AI Documentation

Extraction & Chunking Strategies API
====================================

This documentation covers the API reference for extraction and chunking strategies in Crawl4AI.

Extraction Strategies
---------------------

All extraction strategies inherit from the base `ExtractionStrategy` class and implement two key methods: - `extract(url: str, html: str) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]` - `run(url: str, sections: List[str]) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]`

### LLMExtractionStrategy

Used for extracting structured data using Language Models.

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     # Required Parameters [](#__codelineno-0-3)     provider: str = DEFAULT_PROVIDER,     # LLM provider (e.g., "ollama/llama2") [](#__codelineno-0-4)     api_token: Optional[str] = None,      # API token [](#__codelineno-0-5) [](#__codelineno-0-6)     # Extraction Configuration [](#__codelineno-0-7)     instruction: str = None,              # Custom extraction instruction [](#__codelineno-0-8)     schema: Dict = None,                  # Pydantic model schema for structured data [](#__codelineno-0-9)     extraction_type: str = "block",       # "block" or "schema" [](#__codelineno-0-10) [](#__codelineno-0-11)     # Chunking Parameters [](#__codelineno-0-12)     chunk_token_threshold: int = 4000,    # Maximum tokens per chunk [](#__codelineno-0-13)     overlap_rate: float = 0.1,           # Overlap between chunks [](#__codelineno-0-14)     word_token_rate: float = 0.75,       # Word to token conversion rate [](#__codelineno-0-15)     apply_chunking: bool = True,         # Enable/disable chunking [](#__codelineno-0-16) [](#__codelineno-0-17)     # API Configuration [](#__codelineno-0-18)     base_url: str = None,                # Base URL for API [](#__codelineno-0-19)     extra_args: Dict = {},               # Additional provider arguments [](#__codelineno-0-20)     verbose: bool = False                # Enable verbose logging [](#__codelineno-0-21) )`

### CosineStrategy

Used for content similarity-based extraction and clustering.

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     # Content Filtering [](#__codelineno-1-3)     semantic_filter: str = None,        # Topic/keyword filter [](#__codelineno-1-4)     word_count_threshold: int = 10,     # Minimum words per cluster [](#__codelineno-1-5)     sim_threshold: float = 0.3,         # Similarity threshold [](#__codelineno-1-6) [](#__codelineno-1-7)     # Clustering Parameters [](#__codelineno-1-8)     max_dist: float = 0.2,             # Maximum cluster distance [](#__codelineno-1-9)     linkage_method: str = 'ward',       # Clustering method [](#__codelineno-1-10)     top_k: int = 3,                    # Top clusters to return [](#__codelineno-1-11) [](#__codelineno-1-12)     # Model Configuration [](#__codelineno-1-13)     model_name: str = 'sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2',  # Embedding model [](#__codelineno-1-14) [](#__codelineno-1-15)     verbose: bool = False              # Enable verbose logging [](#__codelineno-1-16) )`

### JsonCssExtractionStrategy

Used for CSS selector-based structured data extraction.

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) JsonCssExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     schema: Dict[str, Any],    # Extraction schema [](#__codelineno-2-3)     verbose: bool = False      # Enable verbose logging [](#__codelineno-2-4) ) [](#__codelineno-2-5) [](#__codelineno-2-6) # Schema Structure [](#__codelineno-2-7) schema = { [](#__codelineno-2-8)     "name": str,              # Schema name [](#__codelineno-2-9)     "baseSelector": str,      # Base CSS selector [](#__codelineno-2-10)     "fields": [               # List of fields to extract [](#__codelineno-2-11)         { [](#__codelineno-2-12)             "name": str,      # Field name [](#__codelineno-2-13)             "selector": str,  # CSS selector [](#__codelineno-2-14)             "type": str,     # Field type: "text", "attribute", "html", "regex" [](#__codelineno-2-15)             "attribute": str, # For type="attribute" [](#__codelineno-2-16)             "pattern": str,  # For type="regex" [](#__codelineno-2-17)             "transform": str, # Optional: "lowercase", "uppercase", "strip" [](#__codelineno-2-18)             "default": Any    # Default value if extraction fails [](#__codelineno-2-19)         } [](#__codelineno-2-20)     ] [](#__codelineno-2-21) }`

Chunking Strategies
-------------------

All chunking strategies inherit from `ChunkingStrategy` and implement the `chunk(text: str) -> list` method.

### RegexChunking

Splits text based on regex patterns.

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) RegexChunking( [](#__codelineno-3-2)     patterns: List[str] = None  # Regex patterns for splitting [](#__codelineno-3-3)                                # Default: [r'\n\n'] [](#__codelineno-3-4) )`

### SlidingWindowChunking

Creates overlapping chunks with a sliding window approach.

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) SlidingWindowChunking( [](#__codelineno-4-2)     window_size: int = 100,    # Window size in words [](#__codelineno-4-3)     step: int = 50             # Step size between windows [](#__codelineno-4-4) )`

### OverlappingWindowChunking

Creates chunks with specified overlap.

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) OverlappingWindowChunking( [](#__codelineno-5-2)     window_size: int = 1000,   # Chunk size in words [](#__codelineno-5-3)     overlap: int = 100         # Overlap size in words [](#__codelineno-5-4) )`

Usage Examples
--------------

### LLM Extraction

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) from pydantic import BaseModel [](#__codelineno-6-2) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import LLMExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-6-3) [](#__codelineno-6-4) # Define schema [](#__codelineno-6-5) class Article(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-6-6)     title: str [](#__codelineno-6-7)     content: str [](#__codelineno-6-8)     author: str [](#__codelineno-6-9) [](#__codelineno-6-10) # Create strategy [](#__codelineno-6-11) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-6-12)     provider="ollama/llama2", [](#__codelineno-6-13)     schema=Article.schema(), [](#__codelineno-6-14)     instruction="Extract article details" [](#__codelineno-6-15) ) [](#__codelineno-6-16) [](#__codelineno-6-17) # Use with crawler [](#__codelineno-6-18) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-6-19)     url="https://example.com/article", [](#__codelineno-6-20)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-6-21) ) [](#__codelineno-6-22) [](#__codelineno-6-23) # Access extracted data [](#__codelineno-6-24) data = json.loads(result.extracted_content)`

### CSS Extraction

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) from crawl4ai.extraction_strategy import JsonCssExtractionStrategy [](#__codelineno-7-2) [](#__codelineno-7-3) # Define schema [](#__codelineno-7-4) schema = { [](#__codelineno-7-5)     "name": "Product List", [](#__codelineno-7-6)     "baseSelector": ".product-card", [](#__codelineno-7-7)     "fields": [ [](#__codelineno-7-8)         { [](#__codelineno-7-9)             "name": "title", [](#__codelineno-7-10)             "selector": "h2.title", [](#__codelineno-7-11)             "type": "text" [](#__codelineno-7-12)         }, [](#__codelineno-7-13)         { [](#__codelineno-7-14)             "name": "price", [](#__codelineno-7-15)             "selector": ".price", [](#__codelineno-7-16)             "type": "text", [](#__codelineno-7-17)             "transform": "strip" [](#__codelineno-7-18)         }, [](#__codelineno-7-19)         { [](#__codelineno-7-20)             "name": "image", [](#__codelineno-7-21)             "selector": "img", [](#__codelineno-7-22)             "type": "attribute", [](#__codelineno-7-23)             "attribute": "src" [](#__codelineno-7-24)         } [](#__codelineno-7-25)     ] [](#__codelineno-7-26) } [](#__codelineno-7-27) [](#__codelineno-7-28) # Create and use strategy [](#__codelineno-7-29) strategy = JsonCssExtractionStrategy(schema) [](#__codelineno-7-30) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-31)     url="https://example.com/products", [](#__codelineno-7-32)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-7-33) )`

### Content Chunking

`[](#__codelineno-8-1) from crawl4ai.chunking_strategy import OverlappingWindowChunking [](#__codelineno-8-2) [](#__codelineno-8-3) # Create chunking strategy [](#__codelineno-8-4) chunker = OverlappingWindowChunking( [](#__codelineno-8-5)     window_size=500,  # 500 words per chunk [](#__codelineno-8-6)     overlap=50        # 50 words overlap [](#__codelineno-8-7) ) [](#__codelineno-8-8) [](#__codelineno-8-9) # Use with extraction strategy [](#__codelineno-8-10) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-8-11)     provider="ollama/llama2", [](#__codelineno-8-12)     chunking_strategy=chunker [](#__codelineno-8-13) ) [](#__codelineno-8-14) [](#__codelineno-8-15) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-8-16)     url="https://example.com/long-article", [](#__codelineno-8-17)     extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-8-18) )`

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Choose the Right Strategy**
2.  Use `LLMExtractionStrategy` for complex, unstructured content
3.  Use `JsonCssExtractionStrategy` for well-structured HTML
4.  Use `CosineStrategy` for content similarity and clustering
    
5.  **Optimize Chunking**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-9-1) # For long documents [](#__codelineno-9-2) strategy = LLMExtractionStrategy( [](#__codelineno-9-3)     chunk_token_threshold=2000,  # Smaller chunks [](#__codelineno-9-4)     overlap_rate=0.1           # 10% overlap [](#__codelineno-9-5) )`
    
6.  **Handle Errors**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-10-1) try: [](#__codelineno-10-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-10-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-10-4)         extraction_strategy=strategy [](#__codelineno-10-5)     ) [](#__codelineno-10-6)     if result.success: [](#__codelineno-10-7)         content = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-10-8) except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-10-9)     print(f"Extraction failed: {e}")`
    
7.  **Monitor Performance**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-11-1) strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-11-2)     verbose=True,  # Enable logging [](#__codelineno-11-3)     word_count_threshold=20,  # Filter short content [](#__codelineno-11-4)     top_k=5  # Limit results [](#__codelineno-11-5) )`
    

* * *

# 1. Getting Started - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 1: Introduction to Crawl4AI and Basic Installation
----------------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Walk through installation from PyPI, setup, and verification. Show how to install with options like `torch` or `transformer` for advanced capabilities.

Here's a condensed outline of the **Installation and Setup** video content:

* * *

1) **Introduction to Crawl4AI**: Briefly explain that Crawl4AI is a powerful tool for web scraping, data extraction, and content processing, with customizable options for various needs.

2) **Installation Overview**:

*   **Basic Install**: Run `pip install crawl4ai` and `playwright install` (to set up browser dependencies).
    
*   **Optional Advanced Installs**:
    
    *   `pip install crawl4ai[torch]` - Adds PyTorch for clustering.
    *   `pip install crawl4ai[transformer]` - Adds support for LLM-based extraction.
    *   `pip install crawl4ai[all]` - Installs all features for complete functionality.

3) **Verifying the Installation**:

*   Walk through a simple test script to confirm the setup:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) import asyncio [](#__codelineno-0-2) from crawl4ai import AsyncWebCrawler [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-0-5)     async with AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-0-6)         result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com") [](#__codelineno-0-7)         print(result.markdown[:500])  # Show first 500 characters [](#__codelineno-0-8) [](#__codelineno-0-9) asyncio.run(main())`
    
*   Explain that this script initializes the crawler and runs it on a test URL, displaying part of the extracted content to verify functionality.

4) **Important Tips**:

*   **Run** `playwright install` **after installation** to set up dependencies.
*   **For full performance** on text-related tasks, run `crawl4ai-download-models` after installing with `[torch]`, `[transformer]`, or `[all]` options.
*   If you encounter issues, refer to the documentation or GitHub issues.

5) **Wrap Up**:

*   Introduce the next topic in the series, which will cover Crawl4AI's browser configuration options (like choosing between `chromium`, `firefox`, and `webkit`).

* * *

This structure provides a concise, effective guide to get viewers up and running with Crawl4AI in minutes.

* * *

# 2. Advanced Features - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 2: Overview of Advanced Features
----------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

A general overview of advanced features like hooks, CSS selectors, and JSON CSS extraction.

Here's a condensed outline for an **Overview of Advanced Features** video covering Crawl4AI's powerful customization and extraction options:

* * *

### **Overview of Advanced Features**

1) **Introduction to Advanced Features**:

*   Briefly introduce Crawl4AI’s advanced tools, which let users go beyond basic crawling to customize and fine-tune their scraping workflows.

2) **Taking Screenshots**:

*   Explain the screenshot capability for capturing page state and verifying content.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com", screenshot=True)`
    
*   Mention that screenshots are saved as a base64 string in `result`, allowing easy decoding and saving.

3) **Media and Link Extraction**:

*   Demonstrate how to pull all media (images, videos) and links (internal and external) from a page for deeper analysis or content gathering.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com") [](#__codelineno-1-2) print("Media:", result.media) [](#__codelineno-1-3) print("Links:", result.links)`
    

4) **Custom User Agent**:

*   Show how to set a custom user agent to disguise the crawler or simulate specific devices/browsers.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com", user_agent="Mozilla/5.0 (compatible; MyCrawler/1.0)")`
    

5) **Custom Hooks for Enhanced Control**:

*   Briefly cover how to use hooks, which allow custom actions like setting headers or handling login during the crawl.
*   **Example**: Setting a custom header with `before_get_url` hook.
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) async def before_get_url(page): [](#__codelineno-3-2)     await page.set_extra_http_headers({"X-Test-Header": "test"})`
    

6) **CSS Selectors for Targeted Extraction**:

*   Explain the use of CSS selectors to extract specific elements, ideal for structured data like articles or product details.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com", css_selector="h2") [](#__codelineno-4-2) print("H2 Tags:", result.extracted_content)`
    

7) **Crawling Inside Iframes**:

*   Mention how enabling `process_iframes=True` allows extracting content within iframes, useful for sites with embedded content or ads.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-5-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com", process_iframes=True)`
    

8) **Wrap-Up**:

*   Summarize these advanced features and how they allow users to customize every part of their web scraping experience.
*   Tease upcoming videos where each feature will be explored in detail.

* * *

This covers each advanced feature with a brief example, providing a useful overview to prepare viewers for the more in-depth videos.

# 4. Proxy Settings - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 4: Advanced Proxy and Security Settings
-----------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Showcase proxy configurations (HTTP, SOCKS5, authenticated proxies). Demo: Use rotating proxies and set custom headers to avoid IP blocking and enhance security.

Here’s a focused outline for the **Proxy and Security Settings** video:

* * *

### **Proxy & Security Settings**

1) **Why Use Proxies in Web Crawling**:

*   Proxies are essential for bypassing IP-based restrictions, improving anonymity, and managing rate limits.
*   Crawl4AI supports simple proxies, authenticated proxies, and proxy rotation for robust web scraping.

2) **Basic Proxy Setup**:

*   **Using a Simple Proxy**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) # HTTP proxy [](#__codelineno-0-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080") [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) # SOCKS proxy [](#__codelineno-0-5) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(proxy="socks5://proxy.example.com:1080")`
    

3) **Authenticated Proxies**:

*   Use `proxy_config` for proxies requiring a username and password:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) proxy_config = { [](#__codelineno-1-2)     "server": "http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     "username": "user", [](#__codelineno-1-4)     "password": "pass" [](#__codelineno-1-5) } [](#__codelineno-1-6) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(proxy_config=proxy_config)`
    

4) **Rotating Proxies**:

*   Rotating proxies helps avoid IP bans by switching IP addresses for each request:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def get_next_proxy(): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     # Define proxy rotation logic here [](#__codelineno-2-3)     return {"server": "http://next.proxy.com:8080"} [](#__codelineno-2-4) [](#__codelineno-2-5) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-6)     for url in urls: [](#__codelineno-2-7)         proxy = await get_next_proxy() [](#__codelineno-2-8)         crawler.update_proxy(proxy) [](#__codelineno-2-9)         result = await crawler.arun(url=url)`
    
*   This setup periodically switches the proxy for enhanced security and access.

5) **Custom Headers for Additional Security**:

*   Set custom headers to mask the crawler’s identity and avoid detection:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) headers = { [](#__codelineno-3-2)     "X-Forwarded-For": "203.0.113.195", [](#__codelineno-3-3)     "Accept-Language": "en-US,en;q=0.9", [](#__codelineno-3-4)     "Cache-Control": "no-cache", [](#__codelineno-3-5)     "Pragma": "no-cache" [](#__codelineno-3-6) } [](#__codelineno-3-7) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(headers=headers)`
    

6) **Combining Proxies with Magic Mode for Anti-Bot Protection**:

*   For sites with aggressive bot detection, combine `proxy` settings with `magic=True`:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler(proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080", headers={"Accept-Language": "en-US"}) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-4)         magic=True  # Enables anti-detection features [](#__codelineno-4-5)     )`
    
*   **Magic Mode** automatically enables user simulation, random timing, and browser property masking.

7) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Summarize the importance of proxies and anti-detection in accessing restricted content and avoiding bans.
*   Tease the next video: **JavaScript Execution and Handling Dynamic Content** for working with interactive and dynamically loaded pages.

* * *

This outline provides a practical guide to setting up proxies and security configurations, empowering users to navigate restricted sites while staying undetected.

* * *

---

# 5. Dynamic Content - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 5: JavaScript Execution and Dynamic Content Handling
------------------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Explain JavaScript code injection with examples (e.g., simulating scrolling, clicking ‘load more’). Demo: Extract content from a page that uses dynamic loading with lazy-loaded images.

Here’s a focused outline for the **JavaScript Execution and Dynamic Content Handling** video:

* * *

### **JavaScript Execution & Dynamic Content Handling**

1) **Why JavaScript Execution Matters**:

*   Many modern websites load content dynamically via JavaScript, requiring special handling to access all elements.
*   Crawl4AI can execute JavaScript on pages, enabling it to interact with elements like “load more” buttons, infinite scrolls, and content that appears only after certain actions.

2) **Basic JavaScript Execution**:

*   Use `js_code` to execute JavaScript commands on a page:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) # Scroll to bottom of the page [](#__codelineno-0-2) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-3)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-4)     js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);" [](#__codelineno-0-5) )`
    
*   This command scrolls to the bottom, triggering any lazy-loaded or dynamically added content.

3) **Multiple Commands & Simulating Clicks**:

*   Combine multiple JavaScript commands to interact with elements like “load more” buttons:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) js_commands = [ [](#__codelineno-1-2)     "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     "document.querySelector('.load-more').click();" [](#__codelineno-1-4) ] [](#__codelineno-1-5) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-6)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-7)     js_code=js_commands [](#__codelineno-1-8) )`
    
*   This script scrolls down and then clicks the “load more” button, useful for loading additional content blocks.

4) **Waiting for Dynamic Content**:

*   Use `wait_for` to ensure the page loads specific elements before proceeding:
    
    ``[](#__codelineno-2-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-2-4)     wait_for="css:.dynamic-content"  # Wait for elements with class `.dynamic-content` [](#__codelineno-2-5) )``
    
*   This example waits until elements with `.dynamic-content` are loaded, helping to capture content that appears after JavaScript actions.

5) **Handling Complex Dynamic Content (e.g., Infinite Scroll)**:

*   Combine JavaScript execution with conditional waiting to handle infinite scrolls or paginated content:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-3-3)     js_code=[ [](#__codelineno-3-4)         "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-3-5)         "const loadMore = document.querySelector('.load-more'); if (loadMore) loadMore.click();" [](#__codelineno-3-6)     ], [](#__codelineno-3-7)     wait_for="js:() => document.querySelectorAll('.item').length > 10"  # Wait until 10 items are loaded [](#__codelineno-3-8) )`
    
*   This example scrolls and clicks "load more" repeatedly, waiting each time for a specified number of items to load.

6) **Complete Example: Dynamic Content Handling with Extraction**:

*   Full example demonstrating a dynamic load and content extraction in one process:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-4)         js_code=[ [](#__codelineno-4-5)             "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-4-6)             "document.querySelector('.load-more').click();" [](#__codelineno-4-7)         ], [](#__codelineno-4-8)         wait_for="css:.main-content", [](#__codelineno-4-9)         css_selector=".main-content" [](#__codelineno-4-10)     ) [](#__codelineno-4-11)     print(result.markdown[:500])  # Output the main content extracted`
    

7) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Recap how JavaScript execution allows access to dynamic content, enabling powerful interactions.
*   Tease the next video: **Content Cleaning and Fit Markdown** to show how Crawl4AI can extract only the most relevant content from complex pages.

* * *

This outline explains how to handle dynamic content and JavaScript-based interactions effectively, enabling users to scrape and interact with complex, modern websites.

* * *
