# AsyncWebCrawler - Crawl4AI Documentation

AsyncWebCrawler
===============

The `AsyncWebCrawler` class is the main interface for web crawling operations. It provides asynchronous web crawling capabilities with extensive configuration options.

Constructor
-----------

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     # Browser Settings [](#__codelineno-0-3)     browser_type: str = "chromium",         # Options: "chromium", "firefox", "webkit" [](#__codelineno-0-4)     headless: bool = True,                  # Run browser in headless mode [](#__codelineno-0-5)     verbose: bool = False,                  # Enable verbose logging [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7)     # Cache Settings [](#__codelineno-0-8)     always_by_pass_cache: bool = False,     # Always bypass cache [](#__codelineno-0-9)     base_directory: str = str(os.getenv("CRAWL4_AI_BASE_DIRECTORY", Path.home())), # Base directory for cache [](#__codelineno-0-10) [](#__codelineno-0-11)     # Network Settings [](#__codelineno-0-12)     proxy: str = None,                      # Simple proxy URL [](#__codelineno-0-13)     proxy_config: Dict = None,              # Advanced proxy configuration [](#__codelineno-0-14) [](#__codelineno-0-15)     # Browser Behavior [](#__codelineno-0-16)     sleep_on_close: bool = False,           # Wait before closing browser [](#__codelineno-0-17) [](#__codelineno-0-18)     # Custom Settings [](#__codelineno-0-19)     user_agent: str = None,                 # Custom user agent [](#__codelineno-0-20)     headers: Dict[str, str] = {},           # Custom HTTP headers [](#__codelineno-0-21)     js_code: Union[str, List[str]] = None,  # Default JavaScript to execute [](#__codelineno-0-22) )`

### Parameters in Detail

#### Browser Settings

*   **browser\_type** (str, optional)
*   Default: `"chromium"`
*   Options: `"chromium"`, `"firefox"`, `"webkit"`
*   Controls which browser engine to use
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) # Example: Using Firefox [](#__codelineno-1-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="firefox")`
    
*   **headless** (bool, optional)
    
*   Default: `True`
*   When `True`, browser runs without GUI
*   Set to `False` for debugging
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) # Visible browser for debugging [](#__codelineno-2-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(headless=False)`
    
*   **verbose** (bool, optional)
    
*   Default: `False`
*   Enables detailed logging
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) # Enable detailed logging [](#__codelineno-3-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True)`
    

#### Cache Settings

*   **always\_by\_pass\_cache** (bool, optional)
*   Default: `False`
*   When `True`, always fetches fresh content
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) # Always fetch fresh content [](#__codelineno-4-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(always_by_pass_cache=True)`
    
*   **base\_directory** (str, optional)
    
*   Default: User's home directory
*   Base path for cache storage
    
    `[](#__codelineno-5-1) # Custom cache directory [](#__codelineno-5-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(base_directory="/path/to/cache")`
    

#### Network Settings

*   **proxy** (str, optional)
*   Simple proxy URL
    
    `[](#__codelineno-6-1) # Using simple proxy [](#__codelineno-6-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080")`
    
*   **proxy\_config** (Dict, optional)
    
*   Advanced proxy configuration with authentication
    
    `[](#__codelineno-7-1) # Advanced proxy with auth [](#__codelineno-7-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(proxy_config={ [](#__codelineno-7-3)     "server": "http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-7-4)     "username": "user", [](#__codelineno-7-5)     "password": "pass" [](#__codelineno-7-6) })`
    

#### Browser Behavior

*   **sleep\_on\_close** (bool, optional)
*   Default: `False`
*   Adds delay before closing browser
    
    `[](#__codelineno-8-1) # Wait before closing [](#__codelineno-8-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(sleep_on_close=True)`
    

#### Custom Settings

*   **user\_agent** (str, optional)
*   Custom user agent string
    
    `[](#__codelineno-9-1) # Custom user agent [](#__codelineno-9-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-9-3)     user_agent="Mozilla/5.0 (Custom Agent) Chrome/90.0" [](#__codelineno-9-4) )`
    
*   **headers** (Dict\[str, str\], optional)
    
*   Custom HTTP headers
    
    `[](#__codelineno-10-1) # Custom headers [](#__codelineno-10-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-10-3)     headers={ [](#__codelineno-10-4)         "Accept-Language": "en-US", [](#__codelineno-10-5)         "Custom-Header": "Value" [](#__codelineno-10-6)     } [](#__codelineno-10-7) )`
    
*   **js\_code** (Union\[str, List\[str\]\], optional)
    
*   Default JavaScript to execute on each page
    
    `[](#__codelineno-11-1) # Default JavaScript [](#__codelineno-11-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-11-3)     js_code=[ [](#__codelineno-11-4)         "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-11-5)         "document.querySelector('.load-more').click();" [](#__codelineno-11-6)     ] [](#__codelineno-11-7) )`
    

Methods
-------

### arun()

The primary method for crawling web pages.

`[](#__codelineno-12-1) async def arun( [](#__codelineno-12-2)     # Required [](#__codelineno-12-3)     url: str,                              # URL to crawl [](#__codelineno-12-4) [](#__codelineno-12-5)     # Content Selection [](#__codelineno-12-6)     css_selector: str = None,              # CSS selector for content [](#__codelineno-12-7)     word_count_threshold: int = 10,        # Minimum words per block [](#__codelineno-12-8) [](#__codelineno-12-9)     # Cache Control [](#__codelineno-12-10)     bypass_cache: bool = False,            # Bypass cache for this request [](#__codelineno-12-11) [](#__codelineno-12-12)     # Session Management [](#__codelineno-12-13)     session_id: str = None,                # Session identifier [](#__codelineno-12-14) [](#__codelineno-12-15)     # Screenshot Options [](#__codelineno-12-16)     screenshot: bool = False,              # Take screenshot [](#__codelineno-12-17)     screenshot_wait_for: float = None,     # Wait before screenshot [](#__codelineno-12-18) [](#__codelineno-12-19)     # Content Processing [](#__codelineno-12-20)     process_iframes: bool = False,         # Process iframe content [](#__codelineno-12-21)     remove_overlay_elements: bool = False, # Remove popups/modals [](#__codelineno-12-22) [](#__codelineno-12-23)     # Anti-Bot Settings [](#__codelineno-12-24)     simulate_user: bool = False,           # Simulate human behavior [](#__codelineno-12-25)     override_navigator: bool = False,      # Override navigator properties [](#__codelineno-12-26)     magic: bool = False,                   # Enable all anti-detection [](#__codelineno-12-27) [](#__codelineno-12-28)     # Content Filtering [](#__codelineno-12-29)     excluded_tags: List[str] = None,       # HTML tags to exclude [](#__codelineno-12-30)     exclude_external_links: bool = False,  # Remove external links [](#__codelineno-12-31)     exclude_social_media_links: bool = False, # Remove social media links [](#__codelineno-12-32) [](#__codelineno-12-33)     # JavaScript Handling [](#__codelineno-12-34)     js_code: Union[str, List[str]] = None, # JavaScript to execute [](#__codelineno-12-35)     wait_for: str = None,                  # Wait condition [](#__codelineno-12-36) [](#__codelineno-12-37)     # Page Loading [](#__codelineno-12-38)     page_timeout: int = 60000,            # Page load timeout (ms) [](#__codelineno-12-39)     delay_before_return_html: float = None, # Wait before return [](#__codelineno-12-40) [](#__codelineno-12-41)     # Extraction [](#__codelineno-12-42)     extraction_strategy: ExtractionStrategy = None  # Extraction strategy [](#__codelineno-12-43) ) -> CrawlResult:`

### Usage Examples

#### Basic Crawling

`[](#__codelineno-13-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-13-2)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com")`

#### Advanced Crawling

`[](#__codelineno-14-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-14-2)     browser_type="firefox", [](#__codelineno-14-3)     verbose=True, [](#__codelineno-14-4)     headers={"Custom-Header": "Value"} [](#__codelineno-14-5) ) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-14-6)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-14-7)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-14-8)         css_selector=".main-content", [](#__codelineno-14-9)         word_count_threshold=20, [](#__codelineno-14-10)         process_iframes=True, [](#__codelineno-14-11)         magic=True, [](#__codelineno-14-12)         wait_for="css:.dynamic-content", [](#__codelineno-14-13)         screenshot=True [](#__codelineno-14-14)     )`

#### Session Management

`[](#__codelineno-15-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-15-2)     # First request [](#__codelineno-15-3)     result1 = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-15-4)         url="https://example.com/login", [](#__codelineno-15-5)         session_id="my_session" [](#__codelineno-15-6)     ) [](#__codelineno-15-7) [](#__codelineno-15-8)     # Subsequent request using same session [](#__codelineno-15-9)     result2 = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-15-10)         url="https://example.com/protected", [](#__codelineno-15-11)         session_id="my_session" [](#__codelineno-15-12)     )`

Context Manager
---------------

AsyncWebCrawler implements the async context manager protocol:

`[](#__codelineno-16-1) async def __aenter__(self) -> 'AsyncWebCrawler': [](#__codelineno-16-2)     # Initialize browser and resources [](#__codelineno-16-3)     return self [](#__codelineno-16-4) [](#__codelineno-16-5) async def __aexit__(self, *args): [](#__codelineno-16-6)     # Cleanup resources [](#__codelineno-16-7)     pass`

Always use AsyncWebCrawler with async context manager:

`[](#__codelineno-17-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-17-2)     # Your crawling code here [](#__codelineno-17-3)     pass`

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Resource Management**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-18-1) # Always use context manager [](#__codelineno-18-2) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-18-3)     # Crawler will be properly cleaned up [](#__codelineno-18-4)     pass`
    
2.  **Error Handling**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-19-1) try: [](#__codelineno-19-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-19-3)         result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-19-4)         if not result.success: [](#__codelineno-19-5)             print(f"Crawl failed: {result.error_message}") [](#__codelineno-19-6) except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-19-7)     print(f"Error: {str(e)}")`
    
3.  **Performance Optimization**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-20-1) # Enable caching for better performance [](#__codelineno-20-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-20-3)     always_by_pass_cache=False, [](#__codelineno-20-4)     verbose=True [](#__codelineno-20-5) )`
    
4.  **Anti-Detection**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-21-1) # Maximum stealth [](#__codelineno-21-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-21-3)     headless=True, [](#__codelineno-21-4)     user_agent="Mozilla/5.0...", [](#__codelineno-21-5)     headers={"Accept-Language": "en-US"} [](#__codelineno-21-6) ) [](#__codelineno-21-7) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-21-8)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-21-9)     magic=True, [](#__codelineno-21-10)     simulate_user=True [](#__codelineno-21-11) )`
    

Note on Browser Types
---------------------

Each browser type has its characteristics:

*   **chromium**: Best overall compatibility
*   **firefox**: Good for specific use cases
*   **webkit**: Lighter weight, good for basic crawling

Choose based on your specific needs:

`[](#__codelineno-22-1) # High compatibility [](#__codelineno-22-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="chromium") [](#__codelineno-22-3) [](#__codelineno-22-4) # Memory efficient [](#__codelineno-22-5) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="webkit")`

* * *

# AsyncWebCrawler.arun() - Crawl4AI Documentation

Complete Parameter Guide for arun()
===================================

The following parameters can be passed to the `arun()` method. They are organized by their primary usage context and functionality.

Core Parameters
---------------

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     url="https://example.com",   # Required: URL to crawl [](#__codelineno-0-3)     verbose=True,               # Enable detailed logging [](#__codelineno-0-4)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED,  # Control cache behavior [](#__codelineno-0-5)     warmup=True                # Whether to run warmup check [](#__codelineno-0-6) )`

Cache Control
-------------

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) from crawl4ai import CacheMode [](#__codelineno-1-2) [](#__codelineno-1-3) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-4)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED,    # Normal caching (read/write) [](#__codelineno-1-5)     # Other cache modes: [](#__codelineno-1-6)     # cache_mode=CacheMode.DISABLED   # No caching at all [](#__codelineno-1-7)     # cache_mode=CacheMode.READ_ONLY  # Only read from cache [](#__codelineno-1-8)     # cache_mode=CacheMode.WRITE_ONLY # Only write to cache [](#__codelineno-1-9)     # cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS     # Skip cache for this operation [](#__codelineno-1-10) )`

Content Processing Parameters
-----------------------------

### Text Processing

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     word_count_threshold=10,                # Minimum words per content block [](#__codelineno-2-3)     image_description_min_word_threshold=5,  # Minimum words for image descriptions [](#__codelineno-2-4)     only_text=False,                        # Extract only text content [](#__codelineno-2-5)     excluded_tags=['form', 'nav'],          # HTML tags to exclude [](#__codelineno-2-6)     keep_data_attributes=False,             # Preserve data-* attributes [](#__codelineno-2-7) )`

### Content Selection

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-2)     css_selector=".main-content",  # CSS selector for content extraction [](#__codelineno-3-3)     remove_forms=True,             # Remove all form elements [](#__codelineno-3-4)     remove_overlay_elements=True,  # Remove popups/modals/overlays [](#__codelineno-3-5) )`

### Link Handling

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-2)     exclude_external_links=True,          # Remove external links [](#__codelineno-4-3)     exclude_social_media_links=True,      # Remove social media links [](#__codelineno-4-4)     exclude_external_images=True,         # Remove external images [](#__codelineno-4-5)     exclude_domains=["ads.example.com"],  # Specific domains to exclude [](#__codelineno-4-6)     social_media_domains=[               # Additional social media domains [](#__codelineno-4-7)         "facebook.com", [](#__codelineno-4-8)         "twitter.com", [](#__codelineno-4-9)         "instagram.com" [](#__codelineno-4-10)     ] [](#__codelineno-4-11) )`

Browser Control Parameters
--------------------------

### Basic Browser Settings

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-5-2)     headless=True,                # Run browser in headless mode [](#__codelineno-5-3)     browser_type="chromium",      # Browser engine: "chromium", "firefox", "webkit" [](#__codelineno-5-4)     page_timeout=60000,          # Page load timeout in milliseconds [](#__codelineno-5-5)     user_agent="custom-agent",    # Custom user agent [](#__codelineno-5-6) )`

### Navigation and Waiting

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-6-2)     wait_for="css:.dynamic-content",  # Wait for element/condition [](#__codelineno-6-3)     delay_before_return_html=2.0,     # Wait before returning HTML (seconds) [](#__codelineno-6-4) )`

### JavaScript Execution

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-7-2)     js_code=[                     # JavaScript to execute (string or list) [](#__codelineno-7-3)         "window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-7-4)         "document.querySelector('.load-more').click();" [](#__codelineno-7-5)     ], [](#__codelineno-7-6)     js_only=False,               # Only execute JavaScript without reloading page [](#__codelineno-7-7) )`

### Anti-Bot Features

### Session Management

### Proxy Configuration

`[](#__codelineno-11-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-11-2)     proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080",     # Simple proxy URL [](#__codelineno-11-3)     proxy_config={                             # Advanced proxy settings [](#__codelineno-11-4)         "server": "http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-11-5)         "username": "user", [](#__codelineno-11-6)         "password": "pass" [](#__codelineno-11-7)     } [](#__codelineno-11-8) )`

Parameter Interactions and Notes
--------------------------------

1.  **Cache and Performance Setup**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-16-1) # Optimal caching for repeated crawls [](#__codelineno-16-2) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-16-3)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED, [](#__codelineno-16-4)     word_count_threshold=10, [](#__codelineno-16-5)     process_iframes=False [](#__codelineno-16-6) )`
    
2.  **Dynamic Content Handling**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-17-1) # Handle lazy-loaded content [](#__codelineno-17-2) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-17-3)     js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-17-4)     wait_for="css:.lazy-content", [](#__codelineno-17-5)     delay_before_return_html=2.0, [](#__codelineno-17-6)     cache_mode=CacheMode.WRITE_ONLY  # Cache results after dynamic load [](#__codelineno-17-7) )`
    
3.  **Content Extraction Pipeline**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-18-1) # Complete extraction setup [](#__codelineno-18-2) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-18-3)     css_selector=".main-content", [](#__codelineno-18-4)     word_count_threshold=20, [](#__codelineno-18-5)     extraction_strategy=my_strategy, [](#__codelineno-18-6)     chunking_strategy=my_chunking, [](#__codelineno-18-7)     process_iframes=True, [](#__codelineno-18-8)     remove_overlay_elements=True, [](#__codelineno-18-9)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED [](#__codelineno-18-10) )`
    

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Performance Optimization**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-19-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-19-2)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED,  # Use full caching [](#__codelineno-19-3)     word_count_threshold=10,      # Filter out noise [](#__codelineno-19-4)     process_iframes=False         # Skip iframes if not needed [](#__codelineno-19-5) )`
    
2.  **Reliable Scraping**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-20-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-20-2)     magic=True,                   # Enable anti-detection [](#__codelineno-20-3)     delay_before_return_html=1.0, # Wait for dynamic content [](#__codelineno-20-4)     page_timeout=60000,          # Longer timeout for slow pages [](#__codelineno-20-5)     cache_mode=CacheMode.WRITE_ONLY  # Cache results after successful crawl [](#__codelineno-20-6) )`
    
3.  **Clean Content**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-21-1) await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-21-2)     remove_overlay_elements=True,  # Remove popups [](#__codelineno-21-3)     excluded_tags=['nav', 'aside'],# Remove unnecessary elements [](#__codelineno-21-4)     keep_data_attributes=False,    # Remove data attributes [](#__codelineno-21-5)     cache_mode=CacheMode.ENABLED   # Use cache for faster processing [](#__codelineno-21-6) )`

# CrawlResult - Crawl4AI Documentation

CrawlResult
===========

The `CrawlResult` class represents the result of a web crawling operation. It provides access to various forms of extracted content and metadata from the crawled webpage.

Class Definition
----------------

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) class CrawlResult(BaseModel): [](#__codelineno-0-2)     """Result of a web crawling operation.""" [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4)     # Basic Information [](#__codelineno-0-5)     url: str                                # Crawled URL [](#__codelineno-0-6)     success: bool                           # Whether crawl succeeded [](#__codelineno-0-7)     status_code: Optional[int] = None       # HTTP status code [](#__codelineno-0-8)     error_message: Optional[str] = None     # Error message if failed [](#__codelineno-0-9) [](#__codelineno-0-10)     # Content [](#__codelineno-0-11)     html: str                              # Raw HTML content [](#__codelineno-0-12)     cleaned_html: Optional[str] = None      # Cleaned HTML [](#__codelineno-0-13)     fit_html: Optional[str] = None          # Most relevant HTML content [](#__codelineno-0-14)     markdown: Optional[str] = None          # HTML converted to markdown [](#__codelineno-0-15)     fit_markdown: Optional[str] = None      # Most relevant markdown content [](#__codelineno-0-16)     downloaded_files: Optional[List[str]] = None  # Downloaded files [](#__codelineno-0-17) [](#__codelineno-0-18)     # Extracted Data [](#__codelineno-0-19)     extracted_content: Optional[str] = None  # Content from extraction strategy [](#__codelineno-0-20)     media: Dict[str, List[Dict]] = {}       # Extracted media information [](#__codelineno-0-21)     links: Dict[str, List[Dict]] = {}       # Extracted links [](#__codelineno-0-22)     metadata: Optional[dict] = None         # Page metadata [](#__codelineno-0-23) [](#__codelineno-0-24)     # Additional Data [](#__codelineno-0-25)     screenshot: Optional[str] = None         # Base64 encoded screenshot [](#__codelineno-0-26)     session_id: Optional[str] = None         # Session identifier [](#__codelineno-0-27)     response_headers: Optional[dict] = None  # HTTP response headers`

Properties and Their Data Structures
------------------------------------

### Basic Information

`[](#__codelineno-1-1) # Access basic information [](#__codelineno-1-2) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-1-3) [](#__codelineno-1-4) print(result.url)          # "https://example.com" [](#__codelineno-1-5) print(result.success)      # True/False [](#__codelineno-1-6) print(result.status_code)  # 200, 404, etc. [](#__codelineno-1-7) print(result.error_message)  # Error details if failed`

### Content Properties

#### HTML Content

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) # Raw HTML [](#__codelineno-2-2) html_content = result.html [](#__codelineno-2-3) [](#__codelineno-2-4) # Cleaned HTML (removed ads, popups, etc.) [](#__codelineno-2-5) clean_content = result.cleaned_html [](#__codelineno-2-6) [](#__codelineno-2-7) # Most relevant HTML content [](#__codelineno-2-8) main_content = result.fit_html`

#### Markdown Content

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) # Full markdown version [](#__codelineno-3-2) markdown_content = result.markdown [](#__codelineno-3-3) [](#__codelineno-3-4) # Most relevant markdown content [](#__codelineno-3-5) main_content = result.fit_markdown`

### Media Content

The media dictionary contains organized media elements:

`[](#__codelineno-4-1) # Structure [](#__codelineno-4-2) media = { [](#__codelineno-4-3)     "images": [ [](#__codelineno-4-4)         { [](#__codelineno-4-5)             "src": str,           # Image URL [](#__codelineno-4-6)             "alt": str,           # Alt text [](#__codelineno-4-7)             "desc": str,          # Contextual description [](#__codelineno-4-8)             "score": float,       # Relevance score (0-10) [](#__codelineno-4-9)             "type": str,          # "image" [](#__codelineno-4-10)             "width": int,         # Image width (if available) [](#__codelineno-4-11)             "height": int,        # Image height (if available) [](#__codelineno-4-12)             "context": str,       # Surrounding text [](#__codelineno-4-13)             "lazy": bool          # Whether image was lazy-loaded [](#__codelineno-4-14)         } [](#__codelineno-4-15)     ], [](#__codelineno-4-16)     "videos": [ [](#__codelineno-4-17)         { [](#__codelineno-4-18)             "src": str,           # Video URL [](#__codelineno-4-19)             "type": str,          # "video" [](#__codelineno-4-20)             "title": str,         # Video title [](#__codelineno-4-21)             "poster": str,        # Thumbnail URL [](#__codelineno-4-22)             "duration": str,      # Video duration [](#__codelineno-4-23)             "description": str    # Video description [](#__codelineno-4-24)         } [](#__codelineno-4-25)     ], [](#__codelineno-4-26)     "audios": [ [](#__codelineno-4-27)         { [](#__codelineno-4-28)             "src": str,           # Audio URL [](#__codelineno-4-29)             "type": str,          # "audio" [](#__codelineno-4-30)             "title": str,         # Audio title [](#__codelineno-4-31)             "duration": str,      # Audio duration [](#__codelineno-4-32)             "description": str    # Audio description [](#__codelineno-4-33)         } [](#__codelineno-4-34)     ] [](#__codelineno-4-35) } [](#__codelineno-4-36) [](#__codelineno-4-37) # Example usage [](#__codelineno-4-38) for image in result.media["images"]: [](#__codelineno-4-39)     if image["score"] > 5:  # High-relevance images [](#__codelineno-4-40)         print(f"High-quality image: {image['src']}") [](#__codelineno-4-41)         print(f"Context: {image['context']}")`

### Link Analysis

The links dictionary organizes discovered links:

`[](#__codelineno-5-1) # Structure [](#__codelineno-5-2) links = { [](#__codelineno-5-3)     "internal": [ [](#__codelineno-5-4)         { [](#__codelineno-5-5)             "href": str,          # URL [](#__codelineno-5-6)             "text": str,          # Link text [](#__codelineno-5-7)             "title": str,         # Title attribute [](#__codelineno-5-8)             "type": str,          # Link type (nav, content, etc.) [](#__codelineno-5-9)             "context": str,       # Surrounding text [](#__codelineno-5-10)             "score": float        # Relevance score [](#__codelineno-5-11)         } [](#__codelineno-5-12)     ], [](#__codelineno-5-13)     "external": [ [](#__codelineno-5-14)         { [](#__codelineno-5-15)             "href": str,          # External URL [](#__codelineno-5-16)             "text": str,          # Link text [](#__codelineno-5-17)             "title": str,         # Title attribute [](#__codelineno-5-18)             "domain": str,        # Domain name [](#__codelineno-5-19)             "type": str,          # Link type [](#__codelineno-5-20)             "context": str        # Surrounding text [](#__codelineno-5-21)         } [](#__codelineno-5-22)     ] [](#__codelineno-5-23) } [](#__codelineno-5-24) [](#__codelineno-5-25) # Example usage [](#__codelineno-5-26) for link in result.links["internal"]: [](#__codelineno-5-27)     print(f"Internal link: {link['href']}") [](#__codelineno-5-28)     print(f"Context: {link['context']}")`

### Metadata

The metadata dictionary contains page information:

`[](#__codelineno-6-1) # Structure [](#__codelineno-6-2) metadata = { [](#__codelineno-6-3)     "title": str,                # Page title [](#__codelineno-6-4)     "description": str,          # Meta description [](#__codelineno-6-5)     "keywords": List[str],       # Meta keywords [](#__codelineno-6-6)     "author": str,              # Author information [](#__codelineno-6-7)     "published_date": str,      # Publication date [](#__codelineno-6-8)     "modified_date": str,       # Last modified date [](#__codelineno-6-9)     "language": str,            # Page language [](#__codelineno-6-10)     "canonical_url": str,       # Canonical URL [](#__codelineno-6-11)     "og_data": Dict,           # Open Graph data [](#__codelineno-6-12)     "twitter_data": Dict       # Twitter card data [](#__codelineno-6-13) } [](#__codelineno-6-14) [](#__codelineno-6-15) # Example usage [](#__codelineno-6-16) if result.metadata: [](#__codelineno-6-17)     print(f"Title: {result.metadata['title']}") [](#__codelineno-6-18)     print(f"Author: {result.metadata.get('author', 'Unknown')}")`

### Extracted Content

Content from extraction strategies:

`[](#__codelineno-7-1) # For LLM or CSS extraction strategies [](#__codelineno-7-2) if result.extracted_content: [](#__codelineno-7-3)     structured_data = json.loads(result.extracted_content) [](#__codelineno-7-4)     print(structured_data)`

### Screenshot

Base64 encoded screenshot:

`[](#__codelineno-8-1) # Save screenshot if available [](#__codelineno-8-2) if result.screenshot: [](#__codelineno-8-3)     import base64 [](#__codelineno-8-4) [](#__codelineno-8-5)     # Decode and save [](#__codelineno-8-6)     with open("screenshot.png", "wb") as f: [](#__codelineno-8-7)         f.write(base64.b64decode(result.screenshot))`

Usage Examples
--------------

### Basic Content Access

`[](#__codelineno-9-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-9-2)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-9-3) [](#__codelineno-9-4)     if result.success: [](#__codelineno-9-5)         # Get clean content [](#__codelineno-9-6)         print(result.fit_markdown) [](#__codelineno-9-7) [](#__codelineno-9-8)         # Process images [](#__codelineno-9-9)         for image in result.media["images"]: [](#__codelineno-9-10)             if image["score"] > 7: [](#__codelineno-9-11)                 print(f"High-quality image: {image['src']}")`

### Complete Data Processing

`[](#__codelineno-10-1) async def process_webpage(url: str) -> Dict: [](#__codelineno-10-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-10-3)         result = await crawler.arun(url=url) [](#__codelineno-10-4) [](#__codelineno-10-5)         if not result.success: [](#__codelineno-10-6)             raise Exception(f"Crawl failed: {result.error_message}") [](#__codelineno-10-7) [](#__codelineno-10-8)         return { [](#__codelineno-10-9)             "content": result.fit_markdown, [](#__codelineno-10-10)             "images": [ [](#__codelineno-10-11)                 img for img in result.media["images"] [](#__codelineno-10-12)                 if img["score"] > 5 [](#__codelineno-10-13)             ], [](#__codelineno-10-14)             "internal_links": [ [](#__codelineno-10-15)                 link["href"] for link in result.links["internal"] [](#__codelineno-10-16)             ], [](#__codelineno-10-17)             "metadata": result.metadata, [](#__codelineno-10-18)             "status": result.status_code [](#__codelineno-10-19)         }`

### Error Handling

`[](#__codelineno-11-1) async def safe_crawl(url: str) -> Dict: [](#__codelineno-11-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-11-3)         try: [](#__codelineno-11-4)             result = await crawler.arun(url=url) [](#__codelineno-11-5) [](#__codelineno-11-6)             if not result.success: [](#__codelineno-11-7)                 return { [](#__codelineno-11-8)                     "success": False, [](#__codelineno-11-9)                     "error": result.error_message, [](#__codelineno-11-10)                     "status": result.status_code [](#__codelineno-11-11)                 } [](#__codelineno-11-12) [](#__codelineno-11-13)             return { [](#__codelineno-11-14)                 "success": True, [](#__codelineno-11-15)                 "content": result.fit_markdown, [](#__codelineno-11-16)                 "status": result.status_code [](#__codelineno-11-17)             } [](#__codelineno-11-18) [](#__codelineno-11-19)         except Exception as e: [](#__codelineno-11-20)             return { [](#__codelineno-11-21)                 "success": False, [](#__codelineno-11-22)                 "error": str(e), [](#__codelineno-11-23)                 "status": None [](#__codelineno-11-24)             }`

Best Practices
--------------

1.  **Always Check Success**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-12-1) if not result.success: [](#__codelineno-12-2)     print(f"Error: {result.error_message}") [](#__codelineno-12-3)     return`
    
2.  **Use fit\_markdown for Articles**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-13-1) # Better for article content [](#__codelineno-13-2) content = result.fit_markdown if result.fit_markdown else result.markdown`
    
3.  **Filter Media by Score**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-14-1) relevant_images = [ [](#__codelineno-14-2)     img for img in result.media["images"] [](#__codelineno-14-3)     if img["score"] > 5 [](#__codelineno-14-4) ]`
    
4.  **Handle Missing Data**
    
    `[](#__codelineno-15-1) metadata = result.metadata or {} [](#__codelineno-15-2) title = metadata.get('title', 'Unknown Title')`
    

* * *

# 6. Magic Mode - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 6: Magic Mode and Anti-Bot Protection
---------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Highlight `Magic Mode` and anti-bot features like user simulation, navigator overrides, and timing randomization. Demo: Access a site with anti-bot protection and show how `Magic Mode` seamlessly handles it.

Here’s a concise outline for the **Magic Mode and Anti-Bot Protection** video:

* * *

### **Magic Mode & Anti-Bot Protection**

1) **Why Anti-Bot Protection is Important**:

*   Many websites use bot detection mechanisms to block automated scraping. Crawl4AI’s anti-detection features help avoid IP bans, CAPTCHAs, and access restrictions.
*   **Magic Mode** is a one-step solution to enable a range of anti-bot features without complex configuration.

2) **Enabling Magic Mode**:

*   Simply set `magic=True` to activate Crawl4AI’s full anti-bot suite:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-3)     magic=True  # Enables all anti-detection features [](#__codelineno-0-4) )`
    
*   This enables a blend of stealth techniques, including masking automation signals, randomizing timings, and simulating real user behavior.

3) **What Magic Mode Does Behind the Scenes**:

*   **User Simulation**: Mimics human actions like mouse movements and scrolling.
*   **Navigator Overrides**: Hides signals that indicate an automated browser.
*   **Timing Randomization**: Adds random delays to simulate natural interaction patterns.
*   **Cookie Handling**: Accepts and manages cookies dynamically to avoid triggers from cookie pop-ups.

4) **Manual Anti-Bot Options (If Not Using Magic Mode)**:

*   For granular control, you can configure individual settings without Magic Mode:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     simulate_user=True,        # Enables human-like behavior [](#__codelineno-1-4)     override_navigator=True    # Hides automation fingerprints [](#__codelineno-1-5) )`
    
*   **Use Cases**: This approach allows more specific adjustments when certain anti-bot features are needed but others are not.

5) **Combining Proxies with Magic Mode**:

*   To avoid rate limits or IP blocks, combine Magic Mode with a proxy:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     headers={"Accept-Language": "en-US"} [](#__codelineno-2-4) ) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-5)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-6)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-7)         magic=True  # Full anti-detection [](#__codelineno-2-8)     )`
    
*   This setup maximizes stealth by pairing anti-bot detection with IP obfuscation.

6) **Example of Anti-Bot Protection in Action**:

*   Full example with Magic Mode and proxies to scrape a protected page:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-3-3)         url="https://example.com/protected-content", [](#__codelineno-3-4)         magic=True, [](#__codelineno-3-5)         proxy="http://proxy.example.com:8080", [](#__codelineno-3-6)         wait_for="css:.content-loaded"  # Wait for the main content to load [](#__codelineno-3-7)     ) [](#__codelineno-3-8)     print(result.markdown[:500])  # Display first 500 characters of the content`
    
*   This example ensures seamless access to protected content by combining anti-detection and waiting for full content load.

7) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Recap the power of Magic Mode and anti-bot features for handling restricted websites.
*   Tease the next video: **Content Cleaning and Fit Markdown** to show how to extract clean and focused content from a page.

* * *

This outline shows users how to easily avoid bot detection and access restricted content, demonstrating both the power and simplicity of Magic Mode in Crawl4AI.

* * *

---

# 7. Content Cleaning - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 7: Content Cleaning and Fit Markdown
--------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Explain content cleaning options, including `fit_markdown` to keep only the most relevant content. Demo: Extract and compare regular vs. fit markdown from a news site or blog.

Here’s a streamlined outline for the **Content Cleaning and Fit Markdown** video:

* * *

### **Content Cleaning & Fit Markdown**

1) **Overview of Content Cleaning in Crawl4AI**:

*   Explain that web pages often include extra elements like ads, navigation bars, footers, and popups.
*   Crawl4AI’s content cleaning features help extract only the main content, reducing noise and enhancing readability.

2) **Basic Content Cleaning Options**:

*   **Removing Unwanted Elements**: Exclude specific HTML tags, like forms or navigation bars:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-0-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-0-3)     word_count_threshold=10,       # Filter out blocks with fewer than 10 words [](#__codelineno-0-4)     excluded_tags=['form', 'nav'], # Exclude specific tags [](#__codelineno-0-5)     remove_overlay_elements=True   # Remove popups and modals [](#__codelineno-0-6) )`
    
*   This example extracts content while excluding forms, navigation, and modal overlays, ensuring clean results.

3) **Fit Markdown for Main Content Extraction**:

*   **What is Fit Markdown**: Uses advanced analysis to identify the most relevant content (ideal for articles, blogs, and documentation).
*   **How it Works**: Analyzes content density, removes boilerplate elements, and maintains formatting for a clear output.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-1-2) main_content = result.fit_markdown  # Extracted main content [](#__codelineno-1-3) print(main_content[:500])  # Display first 500 characters`
    
*   Fit Markdown is especially helpful for long-form content like news articles or blog posts.

4) **Comparing Fit Markdown with Regular Markdown**:

*   **Fit Markdown** returns the primary content without extraneous elements.
*   **Regular Markdown** includes all extracted text in markdown format.
*   Example to show the difference:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) all_content = result.markdown      # Full markdown [](#__codelineno-2-2) main_content = result.fit_markdown # Only the main content [](#__codelineno-2-3) [](#__codelineno-2-4) print(f"All Content Length: {len(all_content)}") [](#__codelineno-2-5) print(f"Main Content Length: {len(main_content)}")`
    
*   This comparison shows the effectiveness of Fit Markdown in focusing on essential content.

5) **Media and Metadata Handling with Content Cleaning**:

*   **Media Extraction**: Crawl4AI captures images and videos with metadata like alt text, descriptions, and relevance scores:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) for image in result.media["images"]: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     print(f"Source: {image['src']}, Alt Text: {image['alt']}, Relevance Score: {image['score']}")`
    
*   **Use Case**: Useful for saving only relevant images or videos from an article or content-heavy page.

6) **Example of Clean Content Extraction in Action**:

*   Full example extracting cleaned content and Fit Markdown:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-4)         word_count_threshold=10, [](#__codelineno-4-5)         excluded_tags=['nav', 'footer'], [](#__codelineno-4-6)         remove_overlay_elements=True [](#__codelineno-4-7)     ) [](#__codelineno-4-8)     print(result.fit_markdown[:500])  # Show main content`
    
*   This example demonstrates content cleaning with settings for filtering noise and focusing on the core text.

7) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Summarize the power of Crawl4AI’s content cleaning features and Fit Markdown for capturing clean, relevant content.
*   Tease the next video: **Link Analysis and Smart Filtering** to focus on analyzing and filtering links within crawled pages.

* * *

This outline covers Crawl4AI’s content cleaning features and the unique benefits of Fit Markdown, showing users how to retrieve focused, high-quality content from web pages.

* * *

---

# 9. Link Analysis - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 9: Link Analysis and Smart Filtering
--------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Walk through internal and external link classification, social media link filtering, and custom domain exclusion. Demo: Analyze links on a website, focusing on internal navigation vs. external or ad links.

Here’s a focused outline for the **Link Analysis and Smart Filtering** video:

* * *

### **Link Analysis & Smart Filtering**

1) **Importance of Link Analysis in Web Crawling**:

*   Explain that web pages often contain numerous links, including internal links, external links, social media links, and ads.
*   Crawl4AI’s link analysis and filtering options help extract only relevant links, enabling more targeted and efficient crawls.

2) **Automatic Link Classification**:

*   Crawl4AI categorizes links automatically into internal, external, and social media links.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-0-2) [](#__codelineno-0-3) # Access internal and external links [](#__codelineno-0-4) internal_links = result.links["internal"] [](#__codelineno-0-5) external_links = result.links["external"] [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Print first few links for each type [](#__codelineno-0-8) print("Internal Links:", internal_links[:3]) [](#__codelineno-0-9) print("External Links:", external_links[:3])`
    

3) **Filtering Out Unwanted Links**:

*   **Exclude External Links**: Remove all links pointing to external sites.
*   **Exclude Social Media Links**: Filter out social media domains like Facebook or Twitter.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     exclude_external_links=True,         # Remove external links [](#__codelineno-1-4)     exclude_social_media_links=True      # Remove social media links [](#__codelineno-1-5) )`
    

4) **Custom Domain Filtering**:

*   **Exclude Specific Domains**: Filter links from particular domains, e.g., ad sites.
*   **Custom Social Media Domains**: Add additional social media domains if needed.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     exclude_domains=["ads.com", "trackers.com"], [](#__codelineno-2-4)     exclude_social_media_domains=["facebook.com", "linkedin.com"] [](#__codelineno-2-5) )`
    

5) **Accessing Link Context and Metadata**:

*   Crawl4AI provides additional metadata for each link, including its text, type (e.g., navigation or content), and surrounding context.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) for link in result.links["internal"]: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     print(f"Link: {link['href']}, Text: {link['text']}, Context: {link['context']}")`
    
*   **Use Case**: Helps users understand the relevance of links based on where they are placed on the page (e.g., navigation vs. article content).

6) **Example of Comprehensive Link Filtering and Analysis**:

*   Full example combining link filtering, metadata access, and contextual information:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-4-4)         exclude_external_links=True, [](#__codelineno-4-5)         exclude_social_media_links=True, [](#__codelineno-4-6)         exclude_domains=["ads.com"], [](#__codelineno-4-7)         css_selector=".main-content"  # Focus only on main content area [](#__codelineno-4-8)     ) [](#__codelineno-4-9)     for link in result.links["internal"]: [](#__codelineno-4-10)         print(f"Internal Link: {link['href']}, Text: {link['text']}, Context: {link['context']}")`
    
*   This example filters unnecessary links, keeping only internal and relevant links from the main content area.

7) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Summarize the benefits of link filtering for efficient crawling and relevant content extraction.
*   Tease the next video: **Custom Headers, Identity Management, and User Simulation** to explain how to configure identity settings and simulate user behavior for stealthier crawls.

* * *

This outline provides a practical overview of Crawl4AI’s link analysis and filtering features, helping users target only essential links while eliminating distractions.

* * *

# 3. Browser Setup - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 3: Browser Configurations & Headless Crawling
-----------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Explain browser options (`chromium`, `firefox`, `webkit`) and settings for headless mode, caching, and verbose logging.

Here’s a streamlined outline for the **Browser Configurations & Headless Crawling** video:

* * *

### **Browser Configurations & Headless Crawling**

1) **Overview of Browser Options**:

*   Crawl4AI supports three browser engines:
    *   **Chromium** (default) - Highly compatible.
    *   **Firefox** - Great for specialized use cases.
    *   **Webkit** - Lightweight, ideal for basic needs.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) # Using Chromium (default) [](#__codelineno-0-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="chromium") [](#__codelineno-0-3) [](#__codelineno-0-4) # Using Firefox [](#__codelineno-0-5) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="firefox") [](#__codelineno-0-6) [](#__codelineno-0-7) # Using WebKit [](#__codelineno-0-8) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="webkit")`
    

2) **Headless Mode**:

*   Headless mode runs the browser without a visible GUI, making it faster and less resource-intensive.
*   To enable or disable:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) # Headless mode (default is True) [](#__codelineno-1-2) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(headless=True) [](#__codelineno-1-3) [](#__codelineno-1-4) # Disable headless mode for debugging [](#__codelineno-1-5) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(headless=False)`
    

3) **Verbose Logging**: - Use `verbose=True` to get detailed logs for each action, useful for debugging:

`[](#__codelineno-2-1) crawler = AsyncWebCrawler(verbose=True)`

4) **Running a Basic Crawl with Configuration**: - Example of a simple crawl with custom browser settings:

`[](#__codelineno-3-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler(browser_type="firefox", headless=True, verbose=True) as crawler: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     result = await crawler.arun(url="https://www.example.com") [](#__codelineno-3-3)     print(result.markdown[:500])  # Show first 500 characters`

\- This example uses Firefox in headless mode with logging enabled, demonstrating the flexibility of Crawl4AI’s setup.

5) **Recap & Next Steps**: - Recap the power of selecting different browsers and running headless mode for speed and efficiency. - Tease the next video: **Proxy & Security Settings** for navigating blocked or restricted content and protecting IP identity.

* * *

This breakdown covers browser configuration essentials in Crawl4AI, providing users with practical steps to optimize their scraping setup.

# 8. Media Handling - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 8: Media Handling: Images, Videos, and Audio
----------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Showcase Crawl4AI’s media extraction capabilities, including lazy-loaded media and metadata. Demo: Crawl a multimedia page, extract images, and show metadata (alt text, context, relevance score).

Here’s a clear and focused outline for the **Media Handling: Images, Videos, and Audio** video:

* * *

### **Media Handling: Images, Videos, and Audio**

1) **Overview of Media Extraction in Crawl4AI**:

*   Crawl4AI can detect and extract different types of media (images, videos, and audio) along with useful metadata.
*   This functionality is essential for gathering visual content from multimedia-heavy pages like e-commerce sites, news articles, and social media feeds.

2) **Image Extraction and Metadata**:

*   Crawl4AI captures images with detailed metadata, including:
    *   **Source URL**: The direct URL to the image.
    *   **Alt Text**: Image description if available.
    *   **Relevance Score**: A score (0–10) indicating how relevant the image is to the main content.
    *   **Context**: Text surrounding the image on the page.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) result = await crawler.arun(url="https://example.com") [](#__codelineno-0-2) [](#__codelineno-0-3) for image in result.media["images"]: [](#__codelineno-0-4)     print(f"Source: {image['src']}") [](#__codelineno-0-5)     print(f"Alt Text: {image['alt']}") [](#__codelineno-0-6)     print(f"Relevance Score: {image['score']}") [](#__codelineno-0-7)     print(f"Context: {image['context']}")`
    
*   This example shows how to access each image’s metadata, making it easy to filter for the most relevant visuals.

3) **Handling Lazy-Loaded Images**:

*   Crawl4AI automatically supports lazy-loaded images, which are commonly used to optimize webpage loading.
*   **Example with Wait for Lazy-Loaded Content**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-2)     url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-1-3)     wait_for="css:img[data-src]",  # Wait for lazy-loaded images [](#__codelineno-1-4)     delay_before_return_html=2.0   # Allow extra time for images to load [](#__codelineno-1-5) )`
    
*   This setup waits for lazy-loaded images to appear, ensuring they are fully captured.

4) **Video Extraction and Metadata**:

*   Crawl4AI captures video elements, including:
    *   **Source URL**: The video’s direct URL.
    *   **Type**: Format of the video (e.g., MP4).
    *   **Thumbnail**: A poster or thumbnail image if available.
    *   **Duration**: Video length, if metadata is provided.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) for video in result.media["videos"]: [](#__codelineno-2-2)     print(f"Video Source: {video['src']}") [](#__codelineno-2-3)     print(f"Type: {video['type']}") [](#__codelineno-2-4)     print(f"Thumbnail: {video.get('poster')}") [](#__codelineno-2-5)     print(f"Duration: {video.get('duration')}")`
    
*   This allows users to gather video content and relevant details for further processing or analysis.

5) **Audio Extraction and Metadata**:

*   Audio elements can also be extracted, with metadata like:
    *   **Source URL**: The audio file’s direct URL.
    *   **Type**: Format of the audio file (e.g., MP3).
    *   **Duration**: Length of the audio, if available.
*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) for audio in result.media["audios"]: [](#__codelineno-3-2)     print(f"Audio Source: {audio['src']}") [](#__codelineno-3-3)     print(f"Type: {audio['type']}") [](#__codelineno-3-4)     print(f"Duration: {audio.get('duration')}")`
    
*   Useful for sites with podcasts, sound bites, or other audio content.

6) **Filtering Media by Relevance**:

*   Use metadata like relevance score to filter only the most useful media content:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) relevant_images = [img for img in result.media["images"] if img['score'] > 5]`
    
*   This is especially helpful for content-heavy pages where you only want media directly related to the main content.

7) **Example: Full Media Extraction with Content Filtering**:

*   Full example extracting images, videos, and audio along with filtering by relevance:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-5-1) async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-5-2)     result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-5-3)         url="https://example.com", [](#__codelineno-5-4)         word_count_threshold=10,  # Filter content blocks for relevance [](#__codelineno-5-5)         exclude_external_images=True  # Only keep internal images [](#__codelineno-5-6)     ) [](#__codelineno-5-7) [](#__codelineno-5-8)     # Display media summaries [](#__codelineno-5-9)     print(f"Relevant Images: {len(relevant_images)}") [](#__codelineno-5-10)     print(f"Videos: {len(result.media['videos'])}") [](#__codelineno-5-11)     print(f"Audio Clips: {len(result.media['audios'])}")`
    
*   This example shows how to capture and filter various media types, focusing on what’s most relevant.

8) **Wrap Up & Next Steps**:

*   Recap the comprehensive media extraction capabilities, emphasizing how metadata helps users focus on relevant content.
*   Tease the next video: **Link Analysis and Smart Filtering** to explore how Crawl4AI handles internal, external, and social media links for more focused data gathering.

* * *

This outline provides users with a complete guide to handling images, videos, and audio in Crawl4AI, using metadata to enhance relevance and precision in multimedia extraction.

* * *

# 12. Session Crawling - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 12: Session-Based Crawling for Dynamic Websites
-------------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Show session management for handling websites with multiple pages or actions (like “load more” buttons). Demo: Crawl a paginated content page, persisting session data across multiple requests.

Here’s a detailed outline for the **Session-Based Crawling for Dynamic Websites** video, explaining why sessions are necessary, how to use them, and providing practical examples and a visual diagram to illustrate the concept.

* * *

### **11\. Session-Based Crawling for Dynamic Websites**

#### **1\. Introduction to Session-Based Crawling**

*   **What is Session-Based Crawling**: Session-based crawling maintains a continuous browsing session across multiple page states, allowing the crawler to interact with a page and retrieve content that loads dynamically or based on user interactions.
*   **Why It’s Needed**:
    *   In static pages, all content is available directly from a single URL.
    *   In dynamic websites, content often loads progressively or based on user actions (e.g., clicking “load more,” submitting forms, scrolling).
    *   Session-based crawling helps simulate user actions, capturing content that is otherwise hidden until specific actions are taken.

#### **2\. Conceptual Diagram for Session-Based Crawling**

`[](#__codelineno-0-1) graph TD [](#__codelineno-0-2)     Start[Start Session] --> S1[Initial State (S1)] [](#__codelineno-0-3)     S1 -->|Crawl| Content1[Extract Content S1] [](#__codelineno-0-4)     S1 -->|Action: Click Load More| S2[State S2] [](#__codelineno-0-5)     S2 -->|Crawl| Content2[Extract Content S2] [](#__codelineno-0-6)     S2 -->|Action: Scroll Down| S3[State S3] [](#__codelineno-0-7)     S3 -->|Crawl| Content3[Extract Content S3] [](#__codelineno-0-8)     S3 -->|Action: Submit Form| S4[Final State] [](#__codelineno-0-9)     S4 -->|Crawl| Content4[Extract Content S4] [](#__codelineno-0-10)     Content4 --> End[End Session]`

*   **Explanation of Diagram**:
    *   **Start**: Initializes the session and opens the starting URL.
    *   **State Transitions**: Each action (e.g., clicking “load more,” scrolling) transitions to a new state, where additional content becomes available.
    *   **Session Persistence**: Keeps the same browsing session active, preserving the state and allowing for a sequence of actions to unfold.
    *   **End**: After reaching the final state, the session ends, and all accumulated content has been extracted.

#### **3\. Key Components of Session-Based Crawling in Crawl4AI**

*   **Session ID**: A unique identifier to maintain the state across requests, allowing the crawler to “remember” previous actions.
*   **JavaScript Execution**: Executes JavaScript commands (e.g., clicks, scrolls) to simulate interactions.
*   **Wait Conditions**: Ensures the crawler waits for content to load in each state before moving on.
*   **Sequential State Transitions**: By defining actions and wait conditions between states, the crawler can navigate through the page as a user would.

#### **4\. Basic Session Example: Multi-Step Content Loading**

*   **Goal**: Crawl an article feed that requires several “load more” clicks to display additional content.
*   **Code**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) async def crawl_article_feed(): [](#__codelineno-1-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-3)         session_id = "feed_session" [](#__codelineno-1-4) [](#__codelineno-1-5)         for page in range(3): [](#__codelineno-1-6)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-7)                 url="https://example.com/articles", [](#__codelineno-1-8)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-1-9)                 js_code="document.querySelector('.load-more-button').click();" if page > 0 else None, [](#__codelineno-1-10)                 wait_for="css:.article", [](#__codelineno-1-11)                 css_selector=".article"  # Target article elements [](#__codelineno-1-12)             ) [](#__codelineno-1-13)             print(f"Page {page + 1}: Extracted {len(result.extracted_content)} articles")`
    
*   **Explanation**:
    *   **session\_id**: Ensures all requests share the same browsing state.
    *   **js\_code**: Clicks the “load more” button after the initial page load, expanding content on each iteration.
    *   **wait\_for**: Ensures articles have loaded after each click before extraction.

#### **5\. Advanced Example: E-Commerce Product Search with Filter Selection**

*   **Goal**: Interact with filters on an e-commerce page to extract products based on selected criteria.
*   **Example Steps**:
    
    1.  **State 1**: Load the main product page.
    2.  **State 2**: Apply a filter (e.g., “On Sale”) by selecting a checkbox.
    3.  **State 3**: Scroll to load additional products and capture updated results.
*   **Code**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) async def extract_filtered_products(): [](#__codelineno-2-2)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-2-3)         session_id = "product_session" [](#__codelineno-2-4) [](#__codelineno-2-5)         # Step 1: Open product page [](#__codelineno-2-6)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-7)             url="https://example.com/products", [](#__codelineno-2-8)             session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-2-9)             wait_for="css:.product-item" [](#__codelineno-2-10)         ) [](#__codelineno-2-11) [](#__codelineno-2-12)         # Step 2: Apply filter (e.g., "On Sale") [](#__codelineno-2-13)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-14)             url="https://example.com/products", [](#__codelineno-2-15)             session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-2-16)             js_code="document.querySelector('#sale-filter-checkbox').click();", [](#__codelineno-2-17)             wait_for="css:.product-item" [](#__codelineno-2-18)         ) [](#__codelineno-2-19) [](#__codelineno-2-20)         # Step 3: Scroll to load additional products [](#__codelineno-2-21)         for _ in range(2):  # Scroll down twice [](#__codelineno-2-22)             result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-2-23)                 url="https://example.com/products", [](#__codelineno-2-24)                 session_id=session_id, [](#__codelineno-2-25)                 js_code="window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);", [](#__codelineno-2-26)                 wait_for="css:.product-item" [](#__codelineno-2-27)             ) [](#__codelineno-2-28)             print(f"Loaded {len(result.extracted_content)} products after scroll")`
    
*   **Explanation**:
    *   **State Persistence**: Each action (filter selection and scroll) builds on the previous session state.
    *   **Multiple Interactions**: Combines clicking a filter with scrolling, demonstrating how the session preserves these actions.

#### **6\. Key Benefits of Session-Based Crawling**

*   **Accessing Hidden Content**: Retrieves data that loads only after user actions.
*   **Simulating User Behavior**: Handles interactive elements such as “load more” buttons, dropdowns, and filters.
*   **Maintaining Continuity Across States**: Enables a sequential process, moving logically from one state to the next, capturing all desired content without reloading the initial state each time.

#### **7\. Additional Configuration Tips**

*   **Manage Session End**: Always conclude the session after the final state to release resources.
*   **Optimize with Wait Conditions**: Use `wait_for` to ensure complete loading before each extraction.
*   **Handling Errors in Session-Based Crawling**: Include error handling for interactions that may fail, ensuring robustness across state transitions.

#### **8\. Complete Code Example: Multi-Step Session Workflow**

*   **Example**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-3-2)     await crawl_article_feed() [](#__codelineno-3-3)     await extract_filtered_products() [](#__codelineno-3-4) [](#__codelineno-3-5) if __name__ == "__main__": [](#__codelineno-3-6)     asyncio.run(main())`
    

#### **9\. Wrap Up & Next Steps**

*   Recap the usefulness of session-based crawling for dynamic content extraction.
*   Tease the next video: **Hooks and Custom Workflow with AsyncWebCrawler** to cover advanced customization options for further control over the crawling process.

* * *

This outline covers session-based crawling from both a conceptual and practical perspective, helping users understand its importance, configure it effectively, and use it to handle complex dynamic content.

* * *

# 11.3. Cosine Strategy - Crawl4AI Documentation

Crawl4AI
========

Episode 11: Extraction Strategies: JSON CSS, LLM, and Cosine
------------------------------------------------------------

### Quick Intro

Introduce JSON CSS Extraction Strategy for structured data, LLM Extraction Strategy for intelligent parsing, and Cosine Strategy for clustering similar content. Demo: Use JSON CSS to scrape product details from an e-commerce site.

Here’s a structured outline for the **Cosine Similarity Strategy** video, covering key concepts, configuration, and a practical example.

* * *

### **10.3 Cosine Similarity Strategy**

#### **1\. Introduction to Cosine Similarity Strategy**

*   The Cosine Similarity Strategy clusters content by semantic similarity, offering an efficient alternative to LLM-based extraction, especially when speed is a priority.
*   Ideal for grouping similar sections of text, this strategy is well-suited for pages with content sections that may need to be classified or tagged, like news articles, product descriptions, or reviews.

#### **2\. Key Configuration Options**

*   **semantic\_filter**: A keyword-based filter to focus on relevant content.
*   **word\_count\_threshold**: Minimum number of words per cluster, filtering out shorter, less meaningful clusters.
*   **max\_dist**: Maximum allowable distance between elements in clusters, impacting cluster tightness.
*   **linkage\_method**: Method for hierarchical clustering, such as `'ward'` (for well-separated clusters).
*   **top\_k**: Specifies the number of top categories for each cluster.
*   **model\_name**: Defines the model for embeddings, such as `sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2`.
*   **sim\_threshold**: Minimum similarity threshold for filtering, allowing control over cluster relevance.

#### **3\. How Cosine Similarity Clustering Works**

*   **Step 1**: Embeddings are generated for each text section, transforming them into vectors that capture semantic meaning.
*   **Step 2**: Hierarchical clustering groups similar sections based on cosine similarity, forming clusters with related content.
*   **Step 3**: Clusters are filtered based on word count, removing those below the `word_count_threshold`.
*   **Step 4**: Each cluster is then categorized with tags, if enabled, providing context to each grouped content section.

#### **4\. Example Use Case: Clustering Blog Article Sections**

*   **Goal**: Group related sections of a blog or news page to identify distinct topics or discussion areas.
*   **Example HTML Sections**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-0-1) "The economy is showing signs of recovery, with markets up this quarter.", [](#__codelineno-0-2) "In the sports world, several major teams are preparing for the upcoming season.", [](#__codelineno-0-3) "New advancements in AI technology are reshaping the tech landscape.", [](#__codelineno-0-4) "Market analysts are optimistic about continued growth in tech stocks."`
    
*   **Code Setup**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-1-1) async def extract_blog_sections(): [](#__codelineno-1-2)     extraction_strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-1-3)         word_count_threshold=15, [](#__codelineno-1-4)         max_dist=0.3, [](#__codelineno-1-5)         sim_threshold=0.2, [](#__codelineno-1-6)         model_name="sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2", [](#__codelineno-1-7)         top_k=2 [](#__codelineno-1-8)     ) [](#__codelineno-1-9)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-1-10)         url = "https://example.com/blog-page" [](#__codelineno-1-11)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-1-12)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-1-13)             extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-1-14)             cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-1-15)         ) [](#__codelineno-1-16)         print(result.extracted_content)`
    
*   **Explanation**:
    
    *   **word\_count\_threshold**: Ensures only clusters with meaningful content are included.
    *   **sim\_threshold**: Filters out clusters with low similarity, focusing on closely related sections.
    *   **top\_k**: Selects top tags, useful for identifying main topics.

#### **5\. Applying Semantic Filtering with Cosine Similarity**

*   **Semantic Filter**: Filters sections based on relevance to a specific keyword, such as “technology” for tech articles.
*   **Example Code**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-2-1) extraction_strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-2-2)     semantic_filter="technology", [](#__codelineno-2-3)     word_count_threshold=10, [](#__codelineno-2-4)     max_dist=0.25, [](#__codelineno-2-5)     model_name="sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2" [](#__codelineno-2-6) )`
    
*   **Explanation**:
    *   **semantic\_filter**: Only sections with high similarity to the “technology” keyword will be included in the clustering, making it easy to focus on specific topics within a mixed-content page.

#### **6\. Clustering Product Reviews by Similarity**

*   **Goal**: Organize product reviews by themes, such as “price,” “quality,” or “durability.”
*   **Example Reviews**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-3-1) "The quality of this product is outstanding and well worth the price.", [](#__codelineno-3-2) "I found the product to be durable but a bit overpriced.", [](#__codelineno-3-3) "Great value for the money and long-lasting.", [](#__codelineno-3-4) "The build quality is good, but I expected a lower price point."`
    
*   **Code Setup**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-4-1) async def extract_product_reviews(): [](#__codelineno-4-2)     extraction_strategy = CosineStrategy( [](#__codelineno-4-3)         word_count_threshold=20, [](#__codelineno-4-4)         max_dist=0.35, [](#__codelineno-4-5)         sim_threshold=0.25, [](#__codelineno-4-6)         model_name="sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2" [](#__codelineno-4-7)     ) [](#__codelineno-4-8)     async with AsyncWebCrawler() as crawler: [](#__codelineno-4-9)         url = "https://example.com/product-reviews" [](#__codelineno-4-10)         result = await crawler.arun( [](#__codelineno-4-11)             url=url, [](#__codelineno-4-12)             extraction_strategy=extraction_strategy, [](#__codelineno-4-13)             cache_mode=CacheMode.BYPASS [](#__codelineno-4-14)         ) [](#__codelineno-4-15)         print(result.extracted_content)`
    
*   **Explanation**:
    
    *   This configuration clusters similar reviews, grouping feedback by common themes, helping businesses understand customer sentiments around particular product aspects.

#### **7\. Performance Advantages of Cosine Strategy**

*   **Speed**: The Cosine Similarity Strategy is faster than LLM-based extraction, as it doesn’t rely on API calls to external LLMs.
*   **Local Processing**: The strategy runs locally with pre-trained sentence embeddings, ideal for high-throughput scenarios where cost and latency are concerns.
*   **Comparison**: With a well-optimized local model, this method can perform clustering on large datasets quickly, making it suitable for tasks requiring rapid, repeated analysis.

#### **8\. Full Code Example for Clustering News Articles**

*   **Code**:
    
    `[](#__codelineno-5-1) async def main(): [](#__codelineno-5-2)     await extract_blog_sections() [](#__codelineno-5-3)     await extract_product_reviews() [](#__codelineno-5-4) [](#__codelineno-5-5) if __name__ == "__main__": [](#__codelineno-5-6)     asyncio.run(main())`
    

#### **9\. Wrap Up & Next Steps**

*   Recap the efficiency and effectiveness of Cosine Similarity for clustering related content quickly.
*   Close with a reminder of Crawl4AI’s flexibility across extraction strategies, and prompt users to experiment with different settings to optimize clustering for their specific content.

* * *

This outline covers Cosine Similarity Strategy’s speed and effectiveness, providing examples that showcase its potential for clustering various content types efficiently.

* * *
